Faraid — Inheritance

Killing as an Impediment to Inheritance: Hanafi Position
Explains the Hanafi rule on killing and the Shafi'i opposing position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on killing as an impediment to inheritance and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Only direct transgressive killing prevents inheritance; legally sanctioned killing does not.

In this lesson, we examine the first impediment: killing. The Hanafi school limits it to direct, transgressive killing. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, extends it to any killing. We will explore the proof and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that only direct, transgressive killing (where qisas or kaffara is wajib) prevents inheritance. Killing by cause (e.g., digging a well) or by legal sanction (e.g., retribution) does not.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any killing, whether transgressive or legally sanctioned, prevents inheritance. This includes killing by retribution, stoning, by a judge's ruling, by a witness, or in self-defense.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'There is nothing for the killer from the inheritance after the owner of the cow.' The Hanafi school interprets the phrase 'after the owner of the cow' as indicating transgression (ta'addi), since the owner of the cow was a transgressor. Thus, the hadith applies only to transgressive killing.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school relies on the general meaning of the hadith. The Hanafi response is that legal killings (e.g., qisas) are permitted or obligated by the Lawgiver, so they cannot be punished with deprivation of inheritance. Restricting the hadith to transgressive killing resolves this conflict.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi fiqh, a person who kills by retribution can still inherit from the victim; in Shafi'i fiqh, he cannot. This affects estate distribution in cases of retribution or legal execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقتل مباشرة واختلاف الدين أو الدار، والكافر يرث بالنسب والسبب كالمسلم، كالبنوة ولو حجب أحدهما فبالحاجب أي فيرث بالحاجب والقتل مباشرة إلخ: [لا تسببا بأن حفر بئرا] أي من حيث المباشرة وهو الذي يتعلق به وجوب القصاص أو الكفارة، وما لا يتعلق به واحد منهما كالقتل بسبب أو بقصاص لا يوجب الحرمان عندنا، وعند الشافعي: يتعلق الحرمان بمطلق القتل، حتى لا يرث عنده إذا قتله بقصاص، أو رجم، أو كان القريب قاضيا، فحكم بذلك، أو شاهدا يشهد به، أو باغيا فقتله، أو شهر عليه سيفا فقتله دفعا، كل ذلك يمنع الإرث عنده، وهذا لا معنى له؛ لأن الشارع أوجب عليه أو أجاز له قتله، والمراد بقوله عليه: "ليس للقاتل شيء من الميراث"، فهو القتل بالتعدي دل عليه قوله عليه: "ليس للقاتل شيء من الميراث بعد صاحب البقرة" أي قاتل كصاحب البقرة، وهو كان متعديا [رمز الحقائق: ٥١٩/٢] واختلاف الدين حتى لا يرث المسلم من الكافر ولا الكافر منه أي الاختلاف بين الإسلام والكفر، لقوله عليه السلام: "لا يرث المسلم الكافر، ولا الكافر المسلم"، وأما اختلاف ملل الكفار كالنصرانية، واليهودية، والمجوسية، وعبادة الوثن، فلا يمنع الإرث حتى يجري التوارث بين اليهود والمجوس والنصارى؛ لأن الكفر كله ملة واحدة. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢٠/٢] أو الدار: والمؤثر في منع الإرث هو الاختلاف حكما، حتى لا يعتبر الحقيقة بدونه، حتى لا يجري الإرث بين المستأمن والذمي في دارنا ولا في دار الحرب، ويجري بينه وبين من هو في داره؛ لأن المستأمن إذا دخل إلينا أو إليهم من أهل داره حكما، وإن كان من غيره حقيقة والدار إنما تختلف باختلاف المنعة والملك كدار الإسلام ودار الحرب، ودارين مختلفين من دار الحرب باختلاف ملكهم لانقطاع الولاية والتناصر فيما بينهم، والإرث يكون بالولاية. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢٠/٢] والكافر يرث إلخ: أي الكافر يرث بالنسب كالبنوة، والسبب كالزوجية إذا كانت غير محرمة؛ لأنه مختار مكلف فيملك بالأسباب الموضوعة للملك كالمسلم، ولأنه بعقد الذمة التحق مجوسي بالمسملم في المعاملة، فيملك بالأسباب الموضوعة كالمسلم فيكون حكمه في ذلك كحكم المسلم. (عيني) ولو حجب أحدهما: أي لو حجب أحد السببين أي إحدى القرابتين الأخرى بالحاجب، أراد أنه إذا اجتمع في الكافر قرابتان لو تفرقتا في شخصين حجب أحدهما الآخر يرث بالحاجب، وإن لم يحجب يرث بالقرابتين كما إذا تزوج أمه، فولدت له ابنا فهذا الولد ابنها وابن ابنها، فيرث منها إذا ماتت على أنه ابن، ولا يرث على أنه ابن الابن؛ لأن ابن الابن يحجب بالابن ولو ولدت له بنتا مكان الابن ترث الثلثين النصف على أنها بنت، والسدس على أنها بنت الابن تكملة للثلثين وترث من أبيها على أنها بنت ولا ترث على أنها أخت من أم؛ لأن الأخت تسقط بالبنت وهو قول عامة الصحابة رضي الله عنهم وبه أخذ أصحابنا، وفي رواية عن ابن مسعود وزيد بن ثابت رضي الله عنهما أن الكافر يرث بأثبت القرابتين أي بأقواهما وبه أخذ مالك والشافعي، والصحيح الأول. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢٠/٢]
And direct killing, and difference of religion or abode, and the disbeliever inherits by lineage and cause like the Muslim, like sonship. And if one of the two causes blocks the other, then [he inherits] through the blocker. That is, he inherits through the blocker. And direct killing etc.: [not causing by digging a well] i.e., in terms of directness, which is that with which the obligation of retribution or expiation is connected, and what is not connected with either of them, like killing by cause or by retribution, does not cause deprivation according to us. According to al-Shafi'i: deprivation is connected with absolute killing, so that he does not inherit according to him if he killed him by retribution, or stoning, or if the relative was a judge and so ruled, or a witness testifying to it, or a rebel so he killed him, or he drew a sword against him so he killed him in defense—all of that prevents inheritance according to him. And this has no meaning because the Lawgiver obligated him or permitted him to kill him. And the meaning of his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is nothing for the killer from the inheritance' is the killing by transgression, as indicated by his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is nothing for the killer from the inheritance after the owner of the cow,' i.e., a killer like the owner of the cow, and he was transgressing. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:519) And difference of religion: so that the Muslim does not inherit from the disbeliever nor the disbeliever from him—i.e., the difference between Islam and disbelief—due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The Muslim does not inherit from the disbeliever, nor the disbeliever from the Muslim.' As for difference among the religions of the disbelievers, like Christianity, Judaism, Zoroastrianism, and idol worship, it does not prevent inheritance, so inheritance takes place between Jews, Zoroastrians, and Christians because all disbelief is one religion. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:520) Or the abode: and the effective factor in preventing inheritance is the difference in legal status, so that the actuality is not considered without it, so that inheritance does not occur between a musta'min and a dhimmi in our abode nor in the abode of war, and it does occur between him and the one in his abode because the musta'min when he enters to us or to them is from the people of his abode legally, even if he is from others in reality. And the abode differs according to the difference in protection and sovereignty, like the abode of Islam and the abode of war, and two different abodes within the abode of war differ by their sovereignty due to the severance of authority and mutual support between them, and inheritance is by authority. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:520) And the disbeliever inherits, etc.: i.e., the disbeliever inherits by lineage like sonship, and by cause like marriage if it is not prohibited, because he is a free agent, legally responsible, and he owns by the causes established for ownership like the Muslim, and because by the covenant of protection he is attached to the Muslim in transactions, so he owns by the established causes like the Muslim, thus his ruling in that is like the ruling of the Muslim. ('Ayni) And if one of the two blocks the other: i.e., if one of the two causes, i.e., one of the two relationships, blocks the other by the blocker. He meant that if in a disbeliever two relationships are combined which, if they were in two persons, one would block the other, he inherits through the blocker. And if it does not block, he inherits through both relationships. For example, if he married his mother and she gave birth to a son, this son is her son and her daughter's [sic] son [grandson], so he inherits from her when she dies as a son, and he does not inherit as a grandson because the grandson is blocked by the son. And if she gave birth to a daughter instead of a son, she inherits two-thirds: half as a daughter and a sixth as a daughter of the son [granddaughter] to complete the two-thirds. And she inherits from her father as a daughter and does not inherit as a maternal sister because the sister is dropped by the daughter. This is the statement of the generality of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them), and our companions adopted it. There is a narration from Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd ibn Thabit (may Allah be pleased with them) that the disbeliever inherits by the more confirmed of the two relationships, i.e., the stronger one, and Malik and al-Shafi'i adopted it. The correct is the first. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:520)
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the impediments (ḥajb) to inheritance, specifically addressing the effects of killing, difference of religion, and difference of abode (dār). It begins by stating that direct killing (al-qatl mubāshiratan) prevents inheritance, but indirect killing (like digging a well) does not, according to the Hanafi school. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any killing, even if legal (e.g., by retribution or stoning), prevents inheritance. The Hanafi response is that the prophetic hadith refers to transgressive killing (bi al-taʿaddī), citing the story of the 'owner of the cow.' The passage then explains that difference of religion between Islam and kufr prevents inheritance, but differences among non-Muslim religions do not, because all disbelief is one millah. The third impediment is difference of dār (abode) in a legal sense: a musta'min (protected visitor) and a dhimmi do not inherit from each other if they are in different dārs, but a musta'min inherits from someone in his own dār. This is because inheritance is based on walāyah (authority/solidarity). Next, the passage clarifies that a kāfir inherits by lineage (e.g., as a son) and by cause (e.g., marriage), provided the marriage is not prohibited (like incestuous marriages allowed in Magianism). The author then addresses a scenario where a kāfir has two relationships that would normally be in separate persons, one blocking the other. The rule is that he inherits through the blocker (al-ḥājib), not the blocked one. An example is given: a man marries his mother, and she bears a son. The son inherits from her as a son, not as a grandson (since the son blocks the grandson). If she bears a daughter, she inherits half as a daughter plus a sixth as a granddaughter to complete two-thirds. The passage notes that this is the view of the majority of Companions and the Hanafi school, while a narration from Ibn Masʿūd and Zayd ibn Thābit, followed by Mālik and al-Shāfiʿī, holds that the kāfir inherits by the stronger of the two relationships. The Hanafi position is declared correct (al-ṣaḥīḥ al-awwal).

Key Terms
القتل مباشرة (al-qatl mubāsharatan): Killing by direct action that triggers qisas or kaffara, as opposed to killing by cause (e.g., digging a well).
اختلاف الدين (ikhtilāf al-dīn): Difference between Islam and disbelief, which prevents inheritance. Differences among non-Muslim religions do not prevent.
الحاجب (al-ḥājib): The closer relative who blocks a more distant relative from inheriting. In the example, the son blocks the grandson.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following killings does NOT prevent inheritance?
A) Killing by stabbing in a robbery
B) Killing by legal retribution (qisas)
C) Killing by poisoning
D) Killing by pushing off a cliff

Key Takeaway
Only direct transgressive killing prevents inheritance; legally permitted killings do not.

Inheritance of a Kāfir from Prohibited Marriage
Ruling on kāfir inheritance from prohibited marriage with intra-madhhab ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on inheritance by a kāfir through a prohibited marriage and explain the difference between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of such marriages.

Core Idea
A kāfir inherits by lineage but not through a prohibited marriage; the marriage is invalid or treated as corrupt.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage: 'Not by a prohibited marriage.' The text explains that a disbeliever, such as a Magian, cannot inherit through a marriage that is prohibited by Islamic law, even if they consider it valid. The example given is a Magian father marrying his daughter – she inherits from him by daughterhood, not by marriage. The Hanafi imams differ in their legal characterization of such a marriage, but all agree on the practical ruling. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly allocating inheritance in cases involving non-Muslims with prohibited marital relations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the example
The passage states: 'Not by a prohibited marriage.' The example: a Magian marries his daughter. She inherits from him by daughterhood (lineage), not by the prohibited marriage.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say the marriage is invalid (bāṭil) because it is prohibited. Abu Hanifa says the marriage has a ruling of validity in their own law but is not left upon when he becomes Muslim; thus it is like a corrupt (fāsid) marriage.
The dispute is only about legal characterization; the practical result is the same.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Despite the difference, both views lead to the same practical consequence: the daughter does not inherit as a wife; she inherits solely as a child (by daughterhood).
The thamarah is that no inheritance right is created through the prohibited cause.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that inheritance by a prohibited marriage is not valid. The inheritor takes only through valid lineage.
This is consistent with the principle that inheritance through a cause (sabab) requires the cause to be valid in Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بنكاح محرم، ويرث ولد الزنا واللعان بجهة الأم فقط، ووقف للحمل حظ ابن، ويرث إن خرج أكثره فمات لا أقله، ولا توارث بين الغرقى والحرقى إلا إذا علم ترتيب الموتى. وذو رحم وهو قريب ليس بذي سهم وعصبة، لا بنكاح محرم: أي لا يرث الكافر بنكاح محرم كما إذا تزوج مجوسي بنته، فإنها ترث منه بالبنتية لا بالزوجية أما عندهما؛ فلعدم صحة النكاح، وأما عند الإمام، فإنه وإن كان له حكم الصحة لكن لا يقر عليه إذا أسلم، فكان كالفاسد. (طائي، فتح) بجهة الأم لأن نسبه من جهة الأب منقطع فلا يرث به، ومن جهة الأم ثابت، فيرث به أمه، وإخوته من الأم بالفرض لا غير وكذا ترثه أمه وإخوته فرضا لا غير ولا يتصور أن يرث هو أو يورث بالعصوبة إلا بالولاء أو الولاد، فيرثه من أعتقه أو أعتق أمه أو ولده بالعصوبة وكذا هو يرث معتقه، أو معتق معتقه، أو ولده بذلك [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢٠/٢] ووقف للحمل إلخ: أي إذا ترك الميت امرأته حاملا أو غيرها ممن يرثه ولدها وقف للحمل نصيب ابن واحد عند أبي يوسف وعنه يوقف نصيب ابنين وهو قول محمد؛ لأن ولادة الاثنين معتادة، وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه نصيب أربعة بنين، أو أربع بنات أيهما أكثر؛ لأنه يتصور ولادة أربعة في بطن واحد، فيترك نصيبهم احتياطا، والفتوى على الأول [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢١/٢]
Not by a prohibited marriage, and the child of zina and li'an inherits only through the mother's side. And the suspension for the fetus is the share of one son. And he inherits if the majority of it comes out and then dies, not if the lesser part comes out. And there is no mutual inheritance between the drowned and the burned except if the order of deaths is known. And dhū raḥm is a relative who is not an owner of a fixed share nor an ʿaṣabah. 'Not by a prohibited marriage': i.e., the disbeliever does not inherit by a prohibited marriage, as when a Magian marries his daughter, she inherits from him by daughterhood, not by marriage. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because the marriage is invalid; according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), although it has the ruling of validity, he is not left upon it when he becomes Muslim, so it is like a corrupt (marriage). (Ta'i, Fath) 'Through the mother's side': because his lineage from the father's side is severed, so he does not inherit through it, and from the mother's side it is established, so he inherits through it from his mother and his maternal brothers by fard (prescribed share) only, not otherwise. Similarly, his mother and brothers inherit from him by fard only, and it is not conceivable that he inherits or is inherited from by ʿaṣabah except by walā' or walad (emancipation or paternity). So the one who emancipated him or emancipated his mother or his child inherits from him by ʿaṣabah, and similarly he inherits from his emancipator, or his emancipator's emancipator, or his child by that. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:520) 'And the suspension for the fetus etc.': i.e., if the deceased left his wife pregnant, or another woman who would have a child that inherits from him, there is suspended for the fetus the portion of one son according to Abu Yusuf. And from him it is narrated that the portion of two sons is suspended, which is the statement of Muhammad, because the birth of twins is common. According to Abu Hanifa: it is the portion of four sons or four daughters, whichever is more, because it is possible for four to be born in one womb, so their portion is left as a precaution. The fatwa is on the first. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:521)
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage presents several distinct rulings grouped together. First, it states that a kāfir does not inherit through a prohibited marriage (nikāḥ muḥarram). An example is given: a Magian marries his daughter; she inherits from him as a daughter (lineage), not as a wife (cause). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the marriage is invalid (ʿindahumā li-ʿadam ṣiḥḥat al-nikāḥ). According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage has a ruling of validity but is not confirmed when he becomes Muslim, so it is like a corrupt marriage (fāsid). Second, a child born from zina (adultery) or liʿān (mutual imprecation) inherits only through the mother's side, because the paternal lineage is severed. Such a child inherits from the mother and maternal brothers by fixed shares (furūḍ), and they inherit from him similarly. He cannot be an ʿaṣabah (residuary heir) except through walā' (emancipation by a former master) or walad (fathering a child who is free). Thus, the emancipator or his son may inherit from him by ʿaṣabah. Third, the ruling on suspending inheritance for a fetus (ḥaml) is given: when a deceased leaves a pregnant woman, a portion is suspended for the fetus. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says suspend the share of one son; Muhammad says two sons (since twins are common); Abu Hanifa says suspend the share of four sons or four daughters, whichever is greater (since quadruplets are possible). The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. The passage also mentions the rule for the fetus's survival: if the majority of its body (e.g., chest in normal birth, navel in breech) emerges alive and then dies, it inherits; if only the lesser part emerges, it does not. Finally, the definition of dhū raḥm (uterine relative) is given: a relative who is neither a prescribed sharer (ṣāḥib fard) nor an ʿaṣabah (residuary).

Key Terms
نكاح محرم (nikāḥ muḥarram): A marriage that is prohibited due to blood relationship, affinity, or fosterage; such a marriage does not create inheritance rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a Magian woman married to her father inherits from him as:
A) a wife and a daughter, both shares.
B) a daughter only, not as a wife.
C) a wife only, not as a daughter.
D) she does not inherit at all.

Key Takeaway
In inheritance, a prohibited marriage is a preventer (māniʿ) of inheritance through the marital bond; the heir may still inherit through valid blood relations.

Inheritance of Children of Zina and Li‘ān
Ruling on inheritance rights of children with severed paternal lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the inheritance rights of a child born from zina or li‘ān and identify the relatives through whom they inherit and from whom they are excluded.

Core Idea
A child of zina or li‘ān inherits only through the mother's side; paternal lineage is severed for inheritance purposes.

This lesson covers the second major ruling in the passage: children born from adultery (zina) or from the process of mutual imprecation (li‘ān) have a severed paternal lineage, so they only inherit from the mother and her relatives. However, they can inherit through emancipation (walā') if applicable. Understanding this rule prevents common errors in allocating the estates of such children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for children of zina/li'an
The passage states that such a child inherits only through the mother's side (jihat al-umm) because the paternal lineage is cut off.
This applies to both walad al-zina and walad al-li‘ān.
2
Determine which relatives are included on the mother's side
The child inherits from the mother and maternal brothers (akhwāl) by fixed shares (furūḍ), not by ʿaṣabah. Similarly, the mother and maternal brothers inherit from the child by fixed shares.
They do not inherit as ʿaṣabah (residuaries) because they are not from the paternal line.
3
Note the exception for walā' and walad
Although the child cannot be an ʿaṣabah through paternal lineage, he can inherit by ʿaṣabah through emancipation (walā') or through his own child (walad). For example, the emancipator or the child's own child inherits by ʿaṣabah.
This maintains the principle that walā' creates a valid relationship for inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بنكاح محرم، ويرث ولد الزنا واللعان بجهة الأم فقط، ووقف للحمل حظ ابن، ويرث إن خرج أكثره فمات لا أقله، ولا توارث بين الغرقى والحرقى إلا إذا علم ترتيب الموتى. وذو رحم وهو قريب ليس بذي سهم وعصبة، لا بنكاح محرم: أي لا يرث الكافر بنكاح محرم كما إذا تزوج مجوسي بنته، فإنها ترث منه بالبنتية لا بالزوجية أما عندهما؛ فلعدم صحة النكاح، وأما عند الإمام، فإنه وإن كان له حكم الصحة لكن لا يقر عليه إذا أسلم، فكان كالفاسد. (طائي، فتح) بجهة الأم لأن نسبه من جهة الأب منقطع فلا يرث به، ومن جهة الأم ثابت، فيرث به أمه، وإخوته من الأم بالفرض لا غير وكذا ترثه أمه وإخوته فرضا لا غير ولا يتصور أن يرث هو أو يورث بالعصوبة إلا بالولاء أو الولاد، فيرثه من أعتقه أو أعتق أمه أو ولده بالعصوبة وكذا هو يرث معتقه، أو معتق معتقه، أو ولده بذلك [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢٠/٢] ووقف للحمل إلخ: أي إذا ترك الميت امرأته حاملا أو غيرها ممن يرثه ولدها وقف للحمل نصيب ابن واحد عند أبي يوسف وعنه يوقف نصيب ابنين وهو قول محمد؛ لأن ولادة الاثنين معتادة، وعن أبي حنيفة: أنه نصيب أربعة بنين، أو أربع بنات أيهما أكثر؛ لأنه يتصور ولادة أربعة في بطن واحد، فيترك نصيبهم احتياطا، والفتوى على الأول [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢١/٢]
Not by a prohibited marriage, and the child of zina and li'an inherits only through the mother's side. And the suspension for the fetus is the share of one son. And he inherits if the majority of it comes out and then dies, not if the lesser part comes out. And there is no mutual inheritance between the drowned and the burned except if the order of deaths is known. And dhū raḥm is a relative who is not an owner of a fixed share nor an ʿaṣabah. 'Not by a prohibited marriage': i.e., the disbeliever does not inherit by a prohibited marriage, as when a Magian marries his daughter, she inherits from him by daughterhood, not by marriage. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because the marriage is invalid; according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), although it has the ruling of validity, he is not left upon it when he becomes Muslim, so it is like a corrupt (marriage). (Ta'i, Fath) 'Through the mother's side': because his lineage from the father's side is severed, so he does not inherit through it, and from the mother's side it is established, so he inherits through it from his mother and his maternal brothers by fard (prescribed share) only, not otherwise. Similarly, his mother and brothers inherit from him by fard only, and it is not conceivable that he inherits or is inherited from by ʿaṣabah except by walā' or walad (emancipation or paternity). So the one who emancipated him or emancipated his mother or his child inherits from him by ʿaṣabah, and similarly he inherits from his emancipator, or his emancipator's emancipator, or his child by that. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:520) 'And the suspension for the fetus etc.': i.e., if the deceased left his wife pregnant, or another woman who would have a child that inherits from him, there is suspended for the fetus the portion of one son according to Abu Yusuf. And from him it is narrated that the portion of two sons is suspended, which is the statement of Muhammad, because the birth of twins is common. According to Abu Hanifa: it is the portion of four sons or four daughters, whichever is more, because it is possible for four to be born in one womb, so their portion is left as a precaution. The fatwa is on the first. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:521)
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage presents several distinct rulings grouped together. First, it states that a kāfir does not inherit through a prohibited marriage (nikāḥ muḥarram). An example is given: a Magian marries his daughter; she inherits from him as a daughter (lineage), not as a wife (cause). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the marriage is invalid (ʿindahumā li-ʿadam ṣiḥḥat al-nikāḥ). According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage has a ruling of validity but is not confirmed when he becomes Muslim, so it is like a corrupt marriage (fāsid). Second, a child born from zina (adultery) or liʿān (mutual imprecation) inherits only through the mother's side, because the paternal lineage is severed. Such a child inherits from the mother and maternal brothers by fixed shares (furūḍ), and they inherit from him similarly. He cannot be an ʿaṣabah (residuary heir) except through walā' (emancipation by a former master) or walad (fathering a child who is free). Thus, the emancipator or his son may inherit from him by ʿaṣabah. Third, the ruling on suspending inheritance for a fetus (ḥaml) is given: when a deceased leaves a pregnant woman, a portion is suspended for the fetus. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says suspend the share of one son; Muhammad says two sons (since twins are common); Abu Hanifa says suspend the share of four sons or four daughters, whichever is greater (since quadruplets are possible). The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. The passage also mentions the rule for the fetus's survival: if the majority of its body (e.g., chest in normal birth, navel in breech) emerges alive and then dies, it inherits; if only the lesser part emerges, it does not. Finally, the definition of dhū raḥm (uterine relative) is given: a relative who is neither a prescribed sharer (ṣāḥib fard) nor an ʿaṣabah (residuary).

Key Terms
ولد الزنا (walad al-zinā): Child born from adultery; his paternal lineage is severed, so he only inherits from the mother's side.
ولد اللعان (walad al-liʿān): Child of liʿān (mutual imprecation by spouses); the husband denies paternity, so the child's paternal lineage is severed, and he inherits only from the mother's side.
الولاء (al-walā'): A relationship of emancipation that creates inheritance rights by ʿaṣabah; it is a valid cause for inheritance even for a child of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a child born from li‘ān inherits from:
A) his mother and father equally.
B) his mother and maternal brothers only.
C) his mother only, not even maternal brothers.
D) his father and paternal relatives only.

Key Takeaway
A child of zina or li‘ān has a valid maternal lineage for inheritance but no paternal lineage; the exception is inheritance through emancipation (walā').

Suspension for the Fetus and Inheritance in Simultaneous Death
Rulings on fetus inheritance and simultaneous death with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for suspending inheritance for a fetus, identify the intra-madhhab dispute on the amount, and determine when a fetus inherits based on partial emergence.

Core Idea
When a deceased leaves a pregnant woman, a share is suspended for the fetus; the amount suspended is one son's share (mufta bihi), and the fetus inherits if the majority of its body is born alive.

This lesson covers the final part of the passage: rules regarding a fetus (ḥaml) as a potential heir, and a related rule on simultaneous death (gharaqā and ḥarqā). The passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on how many shares to suspend for the fetus: Abu Yusuf says one son's share, Muhammad says two, and Abu Hanifa says four. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. Additionally, a condition is given: the fetus inherits if the majority of its body emerges alive and then dies; if only the lesser part emerges, it does not inherit. Finally, the rule that there is no mutual inheritance among those who drown or burn simultaneously unless the order of death is known.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on suspending for the fetus
When a man dies leaving a pregnant woman (wife or any woman whose child would inherit from him), a portion of the estate is suspended until the child is born. The amount suspended is the share of one son according to the mufta bihi (Abu Yusuf).
The suspension is a precautionary measure to protect the potential heir's rights.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf: one son's share. Muhammad: two sons' share (because twins are common). Abu Hanifa: four sons or four daughters, whichever is greater (because quadruplets are possible). The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf.
The dispute is about the extent of precaution; the underlying principle is to ensure the fetus receives its due if born alive.
3
Apply the condition for the fetus inheriting
The fetus inherits if the majority of its body (e.g., chest in normal birth, navel in breech) emerges alive and then dies. If only the lesser part emerges, it does not inherit.
This determines whether the fetus is considered a legal person who inherits.
4
Understand the rule on simultaneous death
If multiple people die in the same incident (drowning, fire) and the order of death is unknown, they do not inherit from each other. Inheritance is determined only if the order can be established.
This avoids arbitrary allocation when death order is uncertain.

Commentary
This passage presents several distinct rulings grouped together. First, it states that a kāfir does not inherit through a prohibited marriage (nikāḥ muḥarram). An example is given: a Magian marries his daughter; she inherits from him as a daughter (lineage), not as a wife (cause). According to Abu Hanifa, the marriage has a ruling of validity but is not confirmed when he becomes Muslim, so it is like a corrupt marriage (fāsid). Second, a child born from zina (adultery) or liʿān (mutual imprecation) inherits only through the mother's side, because the paternal lineage is severed. Such a child inherits from the mother and maternal brothers by fixed shares (furūḍ), and they inherit from him similarly. He cannot be an ʿaṣabah (residuary heir) except through walā' (emancipation by a former master) or walad (fathering a child who is free). Thus, the emancipator or his son may inherit from him by ʿaṣabah. Third, the ruling on suspending inheritance for a fetus (ḥaml) is given: when a deceased leaves a pregnant woman, a portion is suspended for the fetus. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says suspend the share of one son; Muhammad says two sons (since twins are common); Abu Hanifa says suspend the share of four sons or four daughters, whichever is greater (since quadruplets are possible). Key Terms
الوقف للحمل (al-waqf li-l-ḥaml): Suspending a portion of the estate for a fetus until birth, to determine if it inherits. The amount suspended is debated among Hanafi imams.
خرج أكثره (kharaja aktharuhu): The majority of the fetus's body emerges during birth; this condition determines whether the fetus is considered to have been born alive for inheritance purposes.
غرقى وحرقى (gharaqā wa ḥaraqā): People who die simultaneously in a drowning or fire incident; they do not inherit from each other unless the order of death is known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the fatwa on the amount to suspend for a fetus is based on the view of:
A) Abu Hanifa (share of four sons or daughters).
B) Abu Yusuf (share of one son).
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani (share of two sons).
D) All views are equally operative.

Key Takeaway
When a deceased leaves a pregnant woman who could bear an heir, suspend the share of one son (mufta bihi); the fetus inherits if the majority of its body emerges alive.

The Ruling on Dhawi al-Arham: Proof and Dispute
States the ruling on Dhawi al-Arham with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Dhawi al-Arham inheritance, cite the primary proof from the hadith of Mi'dan Karib, and explain the tarjih over the opposing school's view.

Core Idea
Dhawi al-Arham inherit when no Quranic share-heir or residuary exists, based on the Prophet's declaration that the maternal uncle is an heir.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi position on distant relatives (Dhawi al-Arham) in inheritance law. The passage establishes that they inherit only when there are no closer heirs, with the exception of spouses in the original view. We will examine the key hadith proof and the disagreement with the Maliki and Shafi'i schools, and understand why the Hanafi view is relied upon for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The passage begins: 'They do not inherit with a share-heir and a residuary except one of the two spouses.' Understand that Dhawi al-Arham are excluded when any Quranic share-heir or residuary exists, except spouses who are not blood relatives.
Spouses are excluded from radd (return) because their inheritance is like a debt.
2
Examine the Proof from Hadith
The Hanafi position relies on the hadith of Mi'dan Karib where the Prophet ﷺ says he inherits from those with no heir and the maternal uncle inherits. Identify the wording and its implication: the maternal uncle, a Dhul-Rahm, inherits when no other heir exists.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
3
Analyze the Opposing School's Position
Malik and al-Shafi'i originally held that Dhawi al-Arham do not inherit; the estate goes to Bayt al-Mal. Their proof is a hadith narrated by al-Miqdad that says 'No inheritance for Dhawi al-Arham, it goes to the treasury.' Understand their reasoning.
This hadith is also ahad, creating a conflict (ta'arud).
4
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi school deems its proof stronger because it aligns with the general principle of not leaving blood relatives without inheritance, and because the opposing hadith is interpreted as applying only when the treasury is just and functional. Note that later Shafi'i scholars like Ibn Surayj also adopted the Hanafi view due to treasury corruption.
The tarjih is also based on practice of Companions like 'Umar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض
بيان ذوي الأرحاء
ولا يرث مع ذي سهم وعصبة سوى أحد الزوجين؛ لعدم الرد عليهما،
و ترتيبهم كترتيب العصبات والترجيح بقرب الدرجة ، ثم يكون الأصل و ادرار . أي ترتيب ذوي الأرحام
لما
روی المقداد
الترجيح
فولد الوارث أولى
فإنه قال: "لا" ميراث لذوي الأرحام، بل يوضع في بيت المال" و به أخذ مالك والشافعي، والأصح ما قلنا؛ بن معد يكرب عن النبي عليا أنه قال: "من ترك مالا ،فلورثته وأنا وارث من لا وارث له أعقل عنه وأرثه والخال وارث من لا وارث له يعقل عنه ويرثه"، رواه أحمد وأبو داود وآخرون، ولغيره من الأحاديث، وعلى هذا كانت الصحابة حتى روي عن عمر له في عما الأم، وخالة أعطى العم الثلثين، والخالة الثلث، وكثير من
أصحاب الشافعي خالفوه منهم ابن شريح ذهبوا إلى توريث ذوي الأرحام، وهو اختيار فقهائهم للفتوى في زماننا لفساد بيت المال وصرفه في غير المصارف رمز الحقائق: ٥٢١/٢]
ولا يرث إلخ : أي لا يرث ذو رحم مع ذي سهم وعصبة سوى أحد الزوجين، فإن ذا الرحم يرث معهما؛ لأن العصبة أولى من ذي الرحم، فكذا الرد على ذي السهام أولى منه؛ لأنهم أقرب إلا الزوجين؛ فإنهما لا قرابة لهما مع الميت وإرثهما نظير الدين، فإن صاحب الدين لا يرد عليه ما فضل بعد قضاء الدين، فكذا لا يرد عليهما ما فضل من فرضهما، على ذلك كان عامة الصحابة، وكان عثمان الله يرد على الزوجين أيضا، وكان زيد بن ثابت نه لا يرى الرد على أحد من ذوي الفروض وما فضل منهم يوضع في بيت المال عنده، وفي "القنية": ويفتي بالرد على الزوجين في زماننا لفساد بيت المال رمز الحقائق: ٥٢٢/٢] كترتيب العصبات فيقدم فروع الميت كأولاد البنات وإن سفلوا، ثم أصوله كالأجداد الفاسدين والجدات الفاسدة وإن علوا، ثم فروع أبويه كأولاد الأخوات وبنات الإخوة، وبني الإخوة لأم وإن نزلوا، ثم فروع جديه وجدتيه كالعمات والأعمام لأم والأخوال والخالات وإن بعدوا فصاروا أربعة أصناف. [رمز الحقائق: ٥٢٢/٢] والترجيح: أي الترجيح بين ذوي الأرحام بقرب الدرجة؛ لأن إرثهم بطريق العصوبة، فيقدم الأقرب على الأبعد في كل صنف منهم كما في العصبات، فيكون بنت البنت أولى من بنت بنت البنت. (عيني، مسكين) ثم بكون الأصل إلخ : أي ثم الترجيح بكون الأصل وارثا إن استووا في الدرجة، فولد الوارث أولى، سواء كان ولد عصبة، أو ولد صاحب فرض كبنت بنت الابن أولى من بنت بنت البنت وابن بنت ابن أولى من ابن بنت بنت؛ لأن الوارث أقوى قرابة من غير الوارث، بدليل تقديمه عليه في استحقاق الإرث، فكان من يدلي به أقوى، وللقوة تأثير في التقديم، ألا تری أن بني الأعيان يقدمون على بني العلات في العصوبة لهذا المعنى. واعلم أن اعتبار كون الأصل وارثا وغير وارث إنما هو في الدرجة الثانية لا غير؛ لأنا إن اعتبرنا هذا في الأعم من الدرجة الثانية والثالثة يلزم عدم ترجيح بنت بنت الابن على بنت بنت البنت؛ لأن البنت العليا بنت صلبية وهي وارثة، وهذا باطل فوجب اعتبار ترجيح ذي رحم أصله الأدنى ،وارث سواء كان ذلك الأصل الأدنى عصبة، أو صاحب فرض على ذي رحم أصله الأدنى أي بلا واسطة غير وارث ملا مسكين، تكملة، فتح)
Book of Inheritance. Explanation of Dhawi al-Arham. They do not inherit with a share-heir and a residuary except one of the two spouses, because there is no return (radd) upon them. Their order is like the order of residuaries, and preference is by proximity of degree, then by the origin being an heir. That is, the order of Dhawi al-Arham. Because of what was narrated by al-Miqdad: he said, 'There is no inheritance for Dhawi al-Arham; rather it is placed in the treasury (Bayt al-Mal).' And Malik and al-Shafi'i took that position. But the soundest is what we say, based on what Mi'dan Karib narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'Whoever leaves wealth, then for his heirs, and I am the heir of one who has no heir—I pay blood-wit for him and inherit from him. The maternal uncle is the heir of one who has no heir—he pays blood-wit for him and inherits from him.' Reported by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and others. And there are other hadiths. Upon this were the Companions, until it was narrated from 'Umar regarding a paternal uncle and maternal aunt: he gave the paternal uncle two-thirds and the maternal aunt one-third. Many of al-Shafi'i's followers opposed him, among them Ibn Surayj; they went to the view of giving inheritance to Dhawi al-Arham, and that is the choice of their jurists for fatwa in our time due to the corruption of the treasury and its being spent in improper channels. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:521] 'They do not inherit' etc.: meaning a Dhul-Rahm does not inherit with a share-heir and a residuary except one of the two spouses. For a Dhul-Rahm inherits with them, because the residuary is more entitled than the Dhul-Rahm; similarly, the return (radd) upon the share-heir is more entitled than on them, because they are closer—except the spouses, for they have no kinship with the deceased and their inheritance is analogous to a debt: the creditor does not have the surplus returned to him after the debt is paid; likewise, what remains of their fixed share is not returned to them. Upon this were the generality of the Companions. 'Uthman used to return to the spouses as well. Zaid ibn Thabit was of the view that there is no return to any of the Quranic share-heirs, and whatever surplus remains is placed in the treasury according to him. In al-Qunyah: 'Fatwa is given with return to the spouses in our time due to the corruption of the treasury.' [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:522] Like the order of residuaries: so the descendants of the deceased are preferred, such as children of daughters, even if they are lower; then his ascendants, such as irregular grandfathers and irregular grandmothers, even if higher; then the descendants of his parents, such as children of sisters, daughters of brothers, and sons of brothers from the mother's side, even if lower; then the descendants of his grandfather and grandmother, such as paternal aunts, paternal uncles from the mother, maternal uncles, and maternal aunts, even if distant. They become four categories. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:522] 'And preference': meaning preference among Dhawi al-Arham by proximity of degree, because their inheritance is through the path of residuary (asabah), so the nearer is preferred over the farther in each category, just as in residuaries, so a daughter's daughter is more entitled than a daughter's daughter's daughter. ('Ayni, Miskin) 'Then by the origin being' etc.: meaning then preference is by the origin being an heir if they are equal in degree. So the child of an heir is more entitled, whether the child is of a residuary or of a share-heir, like a son's daughter's daughter is more entitled than a daughter's daughter's daughter, and a son's daughter's son is more entitled than a daughter's daughter's son, because the heir is of stronger kinship than the non-heir, as evidenced by his being preferred over him in entitlement to inheritance, so the one who is connected through him is stronger. And strength has an effect in preference; do you not see that paternal half-brothers (banu al-a'yan) are preferred over consanguine half-brothers (banu al-'allat) in residuaries for this reason? Know that the consideration of the origin being an heir or not is only in the second degree, not beyond; for if we consider this in general—the second and third degrees—it would necessitate that a son's daughter's daughter not be preferred over a daughter's daughter's daughter, because the higher daughter (bint salbiyya) is an heir, and this is false; so it is necessary to consider the preference of a Dhul-Rahm whose immediate lower origin (asl adna) is an heir, whether that immediate lower origin is a residuary or a share-heir, over a Dhul-Rahm whose immediate lower origin is not an heir. (Miskin, Takmila, Fath)
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Book of Inheritance, specifically explaining the ruling for Dhawi al-Arham (distant relatives who are neither Quranic share-heirs nor residuaries). The text begins by stating the general rule: Dhawi al-Arham do not inherit when there is a Quranic share-heir (dhul-sahm) or a residuary (asabah), except for one of the spouses. The reason is that the spouses are not blood relatives and their inheritance is like a debt, so no surplus is returned to them. The passage then presents a dispute: Malik and al-Shafi'i held that Dhawi al-Arham have no inheritance at all; the estate goes to the public treasury (Bayt al-Mal). However, the Hanafi position, deemed more sound (al-ashah), is that Dhawi al-Arham do inherit when there is no Quranic share-heir or residuary, based on a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ narrated by Mi'dan Karib: the Prophet declared himself and the maternal uncle as heirs for those with no heir. This was the practice of many Companions, including 'Umar who gave two-thirds to a paternal uncle and one-third to a maternal aunt. Later, many Shafi'i scholars like Ibn Surayj also adopted the view of giving inheritance to Dhawi al-Arham due to the corruption of the treasury in their times; this is also the operative fatwa in our time. The passage then details the ranking of Dhawi al-Arham, which follows the same order as residuaries: first, descendants (even lower), then ascendants (irregular grandparents), then descendants of parents, then descendants of grandparents. Preference among them is first by proximity of degree (the nearer is preferred, like a daughter's daughter over a great-granddaughter), then by the origin being an heir (e.g., the child of a residuary or share-heir is preferred over the child of a non-heir). An important nuance: only the immediate lower origin (asl adna) is considered, not higher origins, to avoid absurd implications.

Key Terms
ذوو الأرحام (Dhawi al-Arham): Distant relatives who are neither Quranic share-heirs nor residuaries. They inherit when no closer heirs exist.
الرد (al-Radd): Return of surplus to Quranic share-heirs proportionally when no residuary exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for Dhawi al-Arham inheriting?
A) The Quranic verse on inheritance
B) The hadith of Mi'dan Karib
C) The practice of the Khalifah al-Miqdad
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Dhawi al-Arham inherit when no Quranic share-heir or residuary exists, based on strong hadith evidence, and this is the operative fatwa due to treasury considerations.

Ranking and Preference Among Dhawi al-Arham
Details the ranking and preference rules for Dhawi al-Arham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four categories of Dhawi al-Arham in order of priority and apply the two preference rules: proximity of degree and origin being an heir.

Core Idea
Dhawi al-Arham rank like residuaries: descendants, ascendants, then collateral relatives, with nearer degree and connection to an heir taking priority.

After establishing that Dhawi al-Arham can inherit, we need to know how to distribute the estate among multiple distant relatives. This lesson focuses on their ranking and the two-tier preference system: first by closeness to the deceased (degree), then by whether the connecting relative was an heir or not. The passage explains this in detail, with important nuances.

Guided Path
1
Learn the Four Categories of Dhawi al-Arham
The passage lists four categories in order: (1) descendants of the deceased (e.g., children of daughters), (2) ascendants (irregular grandparents), (3) descendants of parents (e.g., children of sisters), (4) descendants of grandparents (e.g., maternal aunts/uncles). This order mirrors that of residuaries.
Each category takes priority over the next.
2
Apply Preference by Proximity of Degree
Within the same category, the nearer in degree to the deceased is preferred. For example, a daughter's daughter is preferred over a daughter's daughter's daughter (great-granddaughter).
This is like the rule for residuaries.
3
Apply Preference by Origin Being an Heir
If two Dhawi al-Arham are equal in degree, the one whose immediate connecting relative (asl adna) was an heir (either a residuary or a share-heir) is preferred over one whose connecting relative was not an heir. For example, a son's daughter's daughter is preferred over a daughter's daughter's daughter, because the son is an heir, while the daughter is also an heir? Actually, the passage clarifies that the son's daughter's daughter connects through a son (heir) and the daughter's daughter connects through a daughter (heir as well?) Wait, need to analyze carefully. The example given: a son's daughter's daughter (bint ibn al-ibn) is preferred over a daughter's daughter's daughter (bint bint al-bint) because the son's daughter's immediate origin (son's daughter's father? Actually, the asl adna is the son's daughter or the daughter's daughter? The text says: 'ولد الوارث أولى، سواء كان ولد عصبة، أو ولد صاحب فرض كبنت بنت الابن أولى من بنت بنت البنت' This means: the child of an heir (whether the heir is a residuary or a share-heir) is preferred over the child of a non-heir. In the example, a son's daughter's daughter (whose connecting line goes through a son's daughter) vs a daughter's daughter's daughter. The immediate origin for the first is the son's daughter (who is an heir? Actually, a son's daughter is a residuary if no son? But here the son's daughter is an heir as a residuary? The text says 'ولد الوارث' meaning the child of an heir. So we need to identify which connecting relative is the 'origin' (asl). The rule says we look at the immediate lower origin (asl adna). For a son's daughter's daughter, the immediate origin is the son's daughter (the middle person), who is an heir (she inherits as a residuary in absence of son). For a daughter's daughter's daughter, the immediate origin is the daughter's daughter, who is also an heir? Actually, a daughter's daughter is a Dhul-Rahm, not an heir. So the first is preferred. That's the point.
This rule applies only to the second degree, not beyond, to avoid absurdities.

Book of Inheritance. Explanation of Dhawi al-Arham. They do not inherit with a share-heir and a residuary except one of the two spouses, because there is no return (radd) upon them. Their order is like the order of residuaries, and preference is by proximity of degree, then by the origin being an heir. That is, the order of Dhawi al-Arham. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Book of Inheritance, specifically explaining the ruling for Dhawi al-Arham (distant relatives who are neither Quranic share-heirs nor residuaries). The text begins by stating the general rule: Dhawi al-Arham do not inherit when there is a Quranic share-heir (dhul-sahm) or a residuary (asabah), except for one of the spouses. Key Terms
الأصل الأدنى (al-Asl al-Adna): The immediate connecting relative (the one directly linking the Dhul-Rahm to the deceased, without an intermediary).
الترجيح بقرب الدرجة (al-Tarjih bi-Qurb al-Daraja): Preference based on the closeness of the generation link to the deceased; fewer steps means stronger claim.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner

The Six Fixed Shares and Their Denominators
Definition and parsing of fixed shares and denominator rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six fixed shares, state their denominators, explain how to combine denominators from the same or different genera, and apply the rule for determining shares of Dhawi al-Arham when kinship directions differ.

Core Idea
The six Quranic shares form two genera; denominators are combined by halving/doubling within a genus and by LCM between genera.

Faraid (inheritance) begins with fixed shares determined by the Quran. These six shares—half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth—each have a base denominator. But when multiple shares appear together, the denominator must be adjusted. This lesson unpacks the system of makharij (denominators) and explains how to derive a common denominator when shares combine, whether they belong to the same genus or different genera. It also covers a special rule for dividing among Dhawi al-Arham when some relatives trace through the father and others through the mother.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the six shares and their individual denominators
List the six fixed shares: half (1/2), quarter (1/4), eighth (1/8), two-thirds (2/3), third (1/3), and sixth (1/6). Note the base denominators: 2, 4, 8 for the first three; 3, 3, 6 for the last three. The quarter and eighth belong to the same genus as half; third and sixth belong to the same genus as two-thirds.
The third and two-thirds both have a denominator of 3 when alone, but two-thirds is 2/3 and third is 1/3.
2
Group into two genera and understand the pattern
The shares form two genera: the half-group (half, quarter, eighth) and the two-thirds group (two-thirds, third, sixth). Within each group, each successive share is half of the previous (e.g., half = 1/2, quarter = 1/4, eighth = 1/8) or double if going upward. This pattern helps in combining denominators.
The pattern is: starting from the largest share in the group (half or two-thirds), divide by 2 to get the next, and so on.
3
Combine shares from the same genus
When shares from the same genus appear together, the denominator of the smallest share (i.e., the one with the largest denominator) suffices for all. For example, if quarter (1/4) and eighth (1/8) are present, the common denominator is 8 because 1/4 = 2/8 and 1/8 = 1/8. Similarly, third (1/3) and sixth (1/6) use denominator 6.
The rule: the denominator of the smaller fraction (the one with the bigger denominator) becomes the common denominator for all shares in the same genus.
4
Combine shares from different genera
When shares from the two different genera are mixed, the common denominator is the least common multiple (LCM) of their individual denominators. For example, half (1/2, denominator 2) and third (1/3, denominator 3) combine to denominator 6 (LCM of 2 and 3). Half becomes 3/6, third becomes 2/6.
This is the general rule: find the smallest number that is a multiple of all denominators involved.
5
Apply the Dhawi al-Arham rule for differing kinship directions
If some Dhawi al-Arham relatives are connected through the father and others through the mother, and they are equal in degree (i.e., same distance from the deceased), then the father's side gets two-thirds of the estate and the mother's side gets one-third. This is based on a precedent from 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. There is an intra-Hanafi difference regarding whether to consider the number of living branches or the attributes of the original ancestors when dividing among Dhawi al-Arham.
Imam Muhammad's method (considering branches) is the mufta bihi (relied upon) position.

Source Text

بإطلاقه
فلقرابة الأب: أي إذا كان بعض ذوي الأرحام من جهة الأب، وبعضهم من جهة الأم كان لمن هو في جهة الأب الثلثان، ولمن هو من جهة الأم الثلث؛ لما روينا من قضية عمر وابن مسعود اما. تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٨٢/٩] وهذا لا يتصور في الفروع، وإنما يتصور في الأصول والعمات والخالات واعلم أنه ليس هذا على إطلاقه بل هو محمول على ما إذا استووا في الدرجة بقرينة ما سبق من قوله والترجيح بقرب الدرجة"؛ إذ هو شامل لما إذا اختلفت جهة القرابة. (تكملة، فتح وإن اتفق إلخ : أي إن اتفقت صفة الأصول، أي الذين يدلون بهم في الذكورة والأنوثة و لم يختلفوا فيها كانت القسمة على أبدانهم حتى تجعل بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين، والمراد بالأصول المدلى بهم سواء كانوا أصولا لهم أو لم يكونوا تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٨٢/٩] منهم إلخ: أي إن لم تتفق صفة الأصول يعتبر العدد من الفروع المدلون بهم، والصفة من البطن الذي اختلف فيقسم المال على ذلك البطن، فيعتبر عدد كل واحد من ذلك البطن بعدد فروعه، حتى يجعل الذكر الذي في ذلك البطن ذكورا بعدد فروعه والأنثى الواحدة إناثا بعدد فروعها، وتعطى الفروع ميراث الأصول، وإذا كان فينهم بطون مختلفة يقسم المال على أول بطن اختلف على الصفة التي ذكرنا، ثم تجعل الذكور طائفة والإناث طائفة بعد القسمة، فما أصاب الذكور يجمع ويقسم على أول بطن اختلف به ذلك، وكذا ما أصاب الإناث، وهكذا يعمل إلى أن إلى الذين هم أحياء، وهذا قول محمد، وعند أبي يوسف والحسن بن زياد: تعتبر أبدان الفروع، سواء اتفقت صفة الأصول في الذكورة والأنوثة، أو اختلفت تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٨٢/٩] والفروض نصف إلخ : أي الفروض المقدرة في كتاب الله هذه الستة وهي نوعان على التنصيف إن بدأت بالأكثر، أو التضعيف إن بدأت بالأقل، فنقول : النصف ونصفه ونصف نصفه والثلثان ونصفه، ونصف نصفه،
ينتهي
أو نقول: الثمن وضعفه وضعف ضعفه والسدس ،وضعفه وضعف ضعفه تكملة البحر الرائق: ٤٨٣/٩] ومخارجها إلخ : أي مخارج هذه الفروض لا تخلو إما أن يجيء كل فريق منها منفردا أو مختلطا بغيره، فإن جاء منفردا فمخرج كل فرض سميه، وهو المخرج الذي يشاركه في الحروف إلا النصف فإنه من اثنين، وليس له سمي، وذلك مثل الثمن من ثمانية، والسدس من ستة، والثلث من ثلاثة والربع من أربعة، وإن جاء مختلطا بغيره، فلا يخلوا إما أن يختلط كل نوع بنوعه، أو أحد النوعين بالآخر، فإن اختلط كل نوع بنوعه، فمخرج الأقل منه يكون مخرجا للكل؛ لأن ما كان مخرجا الجزء يكون مخرجا لضعفه ولضعف ضعفه كالثمانية مخرج الثمن والربع، أو الستة مخرج السدس والثلث، وإن اختلط أحد النوعين بالنوع الآخر، فمخرجهما من أقل عدد يجمعهما، =
Denominators of the Fixed Shares. And when the direction of kinship differs, then for the kinship of the father is double the kinship of the mother, if the origins agree with equality in degree in the attribute of masculinity and femininity, then the division is upon the persons, otherwise the number from them and the attribute from the womb that differs. The fixed shares are: half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, sixth. Their denominators: two for the half, four for the quarter, eight for the eighth, three for the two-thirds, three for the third, six for the sixth. These three (half, quarter, eighth) are one genus; these three (two-thirds, third, sixth) are another genus. (Commentary:) 'For the kinship of the father' etc.: meaning if some of the Dhawi al-Arham are from the father's side and some from the mother's side, then for those from the father's side two-thirds, and for those from the mother's side one-third; because of what we narrated from the case of 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. This is not conceivable in descendants, but only in ascendants, paternal aunts, and maternal aunts. Know that this is not absolute but is restricted to when they are equal in degree, by the indication of what preceded: 'and preference by proximity of degree'; for it includes when the direction of kinship differs. (Takmila, Fath) 'If the origins agree' etc.: meaning if the attributes of the origins—those through whom they connect—agree in masculinity and femininity and do not differ, then the division is upon their persons, such that among them the male gets the share of two females. The intended meaning is the origins through whom they connect, whether they are ascendants for them or not. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:482) 'Otherwise the number' etc.: meaning if the attributes of the origins do not agree, the number from the branches (furu') connected to them is considered, and the attribute from the womb that differs, so the estate is divided upon that womb. So the number of each one from that womb is considered by the number of his branches, such that the male in that womb is made as males by the number of his branches, and the single female as females by the number of her branches. And the branches are given the inheritance of the origins. If there are multiple different wombs, the estate is divided upon the first womb that differs according to the description we mentioned, then the males are made a group and the females a group after division. What falls to the males is collected and divided upon the first womb that differed, and likewise what falls to the females. And so on until reaching those who are alive. This is the saying of Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad: the persons of the branches are considered, whether the attributes of the origins agree in masculinity and femininity or differ. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:482) 'And the fixed shares: half' etc.: meaning the fixed shares prescribed in the Book of Allah are these six. They are two types: by halving if you start from the larger, or by doubling if you start from the smaller. So we say: half, its half, and its half's half; two-thirds, its half, and its half's half. Or we say: eighth, its double, and its double's double; sixth, its double, and its double's double. (Takmila al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:483) 'And their denominators' etc.: meaning the denominators of these fixed shares are either each type coming alone or mixed with another. If each comes alone, the denominator of each share is its namesake—the denominator that shares with it in letters—except the half, which is from two and has no namesake. For example, the eighth is from eight, the sixth from six, the third from three, the quarter from four. If it is mixed with another, then either each type is mixed with its own type, or one type with the other. If each type is mixed with its own type, the denominator of the smaller is the denominator for all, because whatever is the denominator for the part is the denominator for its double and the double of its double, like eight is the denominator for eighth and quarter; or six is the denominator for sixth and third. If one type is mixed with the other, then their denominator is the least number that combines them.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a technical commentary on the denominators (makharij) of the six fixed Quranic shares (furud) in inheritance law. It begins by discussing a rule for Dhawi al-Arham when the direction of kinship varies: if some are from the father's side and some from the mother's, the father's side gets two-thirds and the mother's one-third, but only if they are equal in degree. This is based on a case from 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. The text then transitions to the method of dividing shares when the origins (through whom Dhawi al-Arham connect) differ in gender. Imam Muhammad's method is to look at the number of branches (descendants) from each origin and the gender attribute from the first differing womb; the estate is divided accordingly by converting each male/female ancestor into multiples based on their branches. Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, however, simply consider the actual persons (bodies) of the living branches, regardless of the gender of the origins. The final part details the six fixed shares: half (nisf), quarter (rub'), eighth (thumn), two-thirds (thuluthan), third (thuluth), sixth (sudus). They form two genera: one descending from half (half, quarter, eighth) and one descending from two-thirds (two-thirds, third, sixth). The denominator for each share when alone is its standard number (2,4,8 for the first genus; 3,3,6 for the second). When shares from the same genus are combined, the smaller denominator suffices for all (e.g., 8 for quarter and eighth; 6 for third and sixth). When shares from different genera are combined, the common denominator is the least number that contains both denominators (e.g., 6 for half and third gives 6: half=3/6, third=2/6). The text cuts off but this principle continues.

Key Terms
مخرج (Makhraj (pl. Makharij)): Denominator of a fixed share; the number from which the share is derived (e.g., 2 for half, 4 for quarter).
فرض (Fard (pl. Furud)): A fixed Quranic share in inheritance, such as half, quarter, etc.
صنف (Sinf (pl. Asnaf)): Genus or category of shares; the six shares are divided into two genera: the half group and the two-thirds group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the common denominator when a quarter (1/4) and an eighth (1/8) are combined?
A) 8
B) 4
C) 16
D) 12

Key Takeaway
The six fixed shares form two genera; when combined, use the denominator of the smallest share within the same genus, and use the LCM when mixing genera.

Dhawi al-Arham: Paternal vs Maternal Shares and Counting Methods
Intra-Hanafi dispute on counting dhawi al-arham shares when gender differs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that paternal dhawi al-arham inherits double the maternal share when degrees are equal, and distinguish between the counting methods of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Paternal side gets double maternal in dhawi al-arham, but counting method splits Muhammad from Abu Yusuf.

When a deceased leaves only non-Quranic heirs (dhawi al-arham) from both paternal and maternal sides, the Hanafi school applies a two-step process: first, a general rule that paternal kinship receives twice the maternal share; second, a detailed counting method to distribute among the heirs. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the rule and the internal Hanafi dispute over how to count when intermediaries differ in gender.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for direction difference
Identify the rule: when some dhawi al-arham are from the father's side and some from the mother's side (and equal in degree), paternal heirs get two-thirds, maternal get one-third. This is based on a Companions' precedent.
This rule applies only when degrees are equal; otherwise, closeness of degree takes precedence.
2
Understand the counting method when intermediaries agree in gender
When the intermediaries (ancestors through whom the claim passes) are all male or all female (same gender), divide the estate directly among those intermediaries with the male getting double the female share.
Intermediaries are the 'usul al-mudla bihim' (connecting ancestors), not necessarily real parents.
3
Learn Muhammad's method when intermediaries differ in gender
When intermediaries differ in gender, Muhammad counts each branch (fur'u) as a unit: a male in that womb is counted as many males as his number of children, a female counted as many females. The estate is first divided over the first differing womb, then further divided down to living heirs.
This emphasizes the gender of the intermediary affects the branch's share.
4
Learn Abu Yusuf's alternative method
Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad always divide by the bodies of the living branches (fur'u) directly, regardless of the intermediaries' gender.
They consider only the actual heirs (living branches) like normal inheritance, ignoring the intermediaries' gender.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Work through a concrete example: if deceased has a son (who died earlier) and a daughter (died earlier), and son left one son, daughter left one son. Under Muhammad, intermediaries differ (male vs female), so count branches: each branch = 1, so two branches, but then gender of intermediary? Actually difficult; the practical difference matters when a branch has multiple children.
Muhammad's method increases the share of a branch with many children relative to a branch with few, if the intermediary is male.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند اختلاف جهة القرابة، فلقرابة الأب ضعف قرابة الأم، وإن اتفق الأصول مع الاستواء في الدرجة في صفة الذكورة والأنوثة فالقسمة على الأبدان، وإلا فالعدد منهم والوصف من بطن اختلف. فلقرابة الأب: أي إذا كان بعض ذوي الأرحام من جهة الأب، وبعضهم من جهة الأم كان لمن هو في جهة الأب الثلثان، ولمن هو من جهة الأم الثلث؛ لما روينا من قضية عمر وابن مسعود. وهذا لا يتصور في الفروع، وإنما يتصور في الأصول والعمات والخالات. واعلم أنه ليس هذا على إطلاقه بل هو محمول على ما إذا استووا في الدرجة بقرينة ما سبق من قوله "والترجيح بقرب الدرجة"؛ إذ هو شامل لما إذا اختلفت جهة القرابة. وإن اتفق إلخ: أي إن اتفقت صفة الأصول، أي الذين يدلون بهم في الذكورة والأنوثة ولم يختلفوا فيها كانت القسمة على أبدانهم حتى تجعل بينهم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين، والمراد بالأصول المدلى بهم سواء كانوا أصولا لهم أو لم يكونوا. منهم إلخ: أي إن لم تتفق صفة الأصول يعتبر العدد من الفروع المدلون بهم، والصفة من البطن الذي اختلف فيقسم المال على ذلك البطن، فيعتبر عدد كل واحد من ذلك البطن بعدد فروعه، حتى يجعل الذكر الذي في ذلك البطن ذكورا بعدد فروعه والأنثى الواحدة إناثا بعدد فروعها، وتعطى الفروع ميراث الأصول، وإذا كان فيهم بطون مختلفة يقسم المال على أول بطن اختلف على الصفة التي ذكرنا، ثم تجعل الذكور طائفة والإناث طائفة بعد القسمة، فما أصاب الذكور يجمع ويقسم على أول بطن اختلف به ذلك، وكذا ما أصاب الإناث، وهكذا يعمل إلى أن ينتهي إلى الذين هم أحياء، وهذا قول محمد، وعند أبي يوسف والحسن بن زياد: تعتبر أبدان الفروع، سواء اتفقت صفة الأصول في الذكورة والأنوثة، أو اختلفت.
And when the direction of kinship differs, then for paternal kinship is double the maternal kinship. And if the intermediaries agree along with equality in degree in the quality of masculinity and femininity, then the division is based on the bodies. Otherwise, the number from them and the quality from the womb that differs. By paternal kinship: meaning if some of the dhawi al-arham are from the father's side and some from the mother's side, then those from the father's side get two-thirds and those from the mother's side get one-third, due to what we narrated from the case of Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. This is not conceivable in the branches (fur'u), but only in the roots (usul) and paternal aunts and maternal aunts. Know that this is not absolute but is limited to when they are equal in degree, by indication of what preceded: 'And preponderance by closeness of degree'; for it includes when the direction of kinship differs. 'If they agree, etc.': meaning if the quality of the intermediaries, i.e., those through whom they claim inheritance, agrees in masculinity and femininity and they do not differ therein, then the division is based on their bodies, so that among them the male gets the share of two females. What is meant by intermediaries are those through whom they claim inheritance, whether they are real ancestors or not. 'Otherwise, etc.': meaning if the quality of the intermediaries does not agree, consideration is given to the number of branches (fur'u) who claim through them, and the quality from the womb that differs; then the estate is divided over that womb. Thus the number of every individual of that womb is considered by the number of his branches, so that the male in that womb is counted as males by the number of his branches, and the single female as females by the number of her branches, and the branches are given the inheritance of the intermediaries. And if there are different wombs, the estate is divided over the first womb that differs according to the description we mentioned. Then the males are made a group and the females a group after the division. What the males receive is gathered and divided over the first womb that differed, and likewise what the females receive. This is done until reaching those who are alive. This is the saying of Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad: the bodies of the branches are considered, whether the quality of the intermediaries agrees in masculinity and femininity or differs.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage explains inheritance rules for non-Quranic heirs (dhawi al-arham) when there is a difference in the direction of kinship (some from paternal side, some from maternal). The author first states a general principle: paternal kinship gets double the share of maternal kinship. This is based on a precedent from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. However, this rule only applies when they are equal in degree; otherwise, closeness of degree takes precedence. The passage then explains two scenarios for when the intermediaries (the connecting ancestors) agree or differ in gender. When they agree (all male or all female), the division is based on the bodies of those intermediaries, treating each male and female as a share—male gets double female. When they differ, the counting is based on the number of branches (fur'u) from each intermediary, and the gender is taken from the womb that differs. This is the method of Imam Muhammad. Abu Yusuf and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad disagree: they always consider the bodies of the living branches (fur'u) directly, regardless of the gender of the intermediaries. The practical difference: under Muhammad's method, if an intermediary has many children, that branch gets more shares; under Abu Yusuf's method, it's based on the count of heirs themselves.

Key Terms
جهة القرابة (jihah al-qarabah): Direction of kinship: whether the heir is related through the paternal side or the maternal side.
ذوي الأرحام (dhawi al-arham): Non-Quranic heirs who are not entitled to prescribed shares nor are residuary heirs; they inherit when no other heirs exist.
الأصول المدلى بهم (al-usul al-mudla bihim): The intermediaries (ancestors) through whom the claim of kinship passes, e.g., mother, father, grandmother, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One half
B) Two-thirds
C) Three-fourths
D) One-third

Key Takeaway
When direction of kinship differs among dhawi al-arham of equal degree, paternal side takes two-thirds and maternal one-third, and the intra-Hanafi dispute on counting method does not affect this primary rule but only the subsequent distribution within each side.

Denominators of Prescribed Shares and Rules for Combining
Listing the six prescribed shares and their denominators, and explaining how to find common denominators when shares of different types are combined.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the common denominator (asl al-masalah) for any combination of the six prescribed shares using the Hanafi method of compatibility (wafq) or direct multiplication.

Core Idea
The common denominator for mixed prescribed shares is found by comparing denominators for compatibility; if compatible, take half of one and multiply by the other; if not, multiply both.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the six prescribed shares have fixed denominators. When heirs from different 'types' of shares are present, you must determine the least common denominator for the entire estate. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the method: first identify the two types (half/quarter/eighth vs. two-thirds/third/sixth), then check for compatibility (wafq) between the denominators. If they share a common factor, use it to reduce the multiplication; if not, multiply the denominators directly. Understanding this method is essential for correctly distributing an estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types and denominators
List the six prescribed shares and their individual denominators: half (2), quarter (4), eighth (8), two-thirds (3), third (3), sixth (6). Note that two-thirds and third share the denominator 3.
2
Determine if mixing is within same type or across types
Shares are grouped into two types: first type (half, quarter, eighth) and second type (two-thirds, third, sixth). Check if the shares present all belong to one type or to both types.
The passage calls this 'سمي' (homonym) for same type and 'اختلاط' (mixing) for different types.
3
Same type: use the smallest denominator
If all shares are from the same type, the denominator of the smallest share suffices for all. For example, if quarter and eighth are present, use 8 (denominator of eighth).
Because the denominator of the smallest share is a multiple of the larger ones.
4
Cross-type: check compatibility (wafq)
When shares from both types are present, examine the two denominators for a common factor. If they are compatible (wafq), take the factor of one and multiply by the whole of the other. For example, half (2) and sixth (6) share factor 2: multiply half of 6 (3) by 2 to get 6.
Compatibility means they share a divisor >1. The factor is half of one denominator if they are compatible by half.
5
No compatibility: multiply directly
If there is no common factor, multiply the two denominators directly. For example, eighth (8) and third (3) have no common factor, so denominator = 8 × 3 = 24.
This yields the least common multiple since they are coprime.

Source Text
