(شرح السراجية) ولو مع الثاني من لا يردّ عليه، فاقسم ما بقي من مخرج فرض من لا يردّ عليه على مسألة من يردّ عليه كزوجة وأربع جدات وست أخوات الأم، وإن لم يستقم، فاضرب سهام من يردّ عليه في مخرج فرض من لا يردّ عليه كأربع زوجات وتسع بنات وست جدات، فإن أصل هذه المسألة أربعة وعشرين لكنها ردية من فرددناها إلى أقل مخارج فرض من لا يرد عليه، وهو الثمانية، فإذا دفعنا ثمنها، وهو ثلاثة إلى الزوجات بقيت.
And if with the first (type) there is one who does not receive radd, and he is one of the two spouses: give his fixed share from the smallest of its bases, then divide the remainder among those who receive radd, like a husband and three daughters; and if it does not work out, then if their heads agree, multiply the concordant part of their heads. (Commentary of al-Sirajiyya) And if with the second (type) there is one who does not receive radd, then divide what remains from the base of the fixed share of the one who does not receive radd according to the problem of those who receive radd, like a wife, four grandmothers, and six maternal sisters; and if it does not work out, then multiply the shares of those who receive radd by the base of the fixed share of the one who does not receive radd, like four wives, nine daughters, and six grandmothers. When we give its eighth, which is three, to the wives, there remains...

Commentary
This passage explains the method of radd (return of surplus) when a spouse (who never receives radd) is present among heirs who are entitled to radd. The text distinguishes two scenarios: (1) when the radd-receiving heirs are of one gender (e.g., all daughters), and (2) when they are of two or more genders (e.g., grandmothers and maternal sisters). In both cases, first give the spouse his/her fixed share using the smallest possible base (e.g., 4 for a husband's 1/4). Then, the remainder is distributed among the radd-receiving heirs according to their respective shares. If the remainder does not divide evenly by the number of heads (i.e., individuals), we look for a common factor (wafq) or multiply all heads by the spouse's base to achieve a whole number. The example of a husband and three daughters: husband gets 1/4 from base 4, 1 share; remainder 3 shares divide evenly among 3 daughters (1 each). If 6 daughters, 3 remainder cannot divide evenly; but 3 and 6 have common factor 3, so we use the concording part (2) and multiply by base 4, resulting in base 8. For the second type, the radd-receiving heirs have different shares (e.g., grandmothers 1/6 each, maternal sisters 1/3 each). The method is similar: give spouse their share, then see if the remainder fits the combined base of the radd heirs. If not, multiply the shares of the radd heirs by the spouse's base. The given example: 4 wives (each gets 1/8), 9 daughters, 6 grandmothers. The original base would be 24, but after giving wives 1/8 (3 shares from base 8), the remainder is 5 shares, which then need to be distributed among daughters and grandmothers. The passage cuts off but the method is clear.

Key Terms
رد (radd): The return of surplus estate to heirs who receive a fixed share (aside from the spouse) when there is no residuary heir.
زوج (zawj): Husband; one of the spouses who does not benefit from radd.
وفق (wafq): Concordance; a common factor between the remainder and the number of heads, used to simplify the base.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a spouse is present along with radd-receiving heirs, what is the first step in distribution?
A) Distribute the entire estate equally among all heirs
B) Give the spouse their fixed share from the smallest base
C) Give the radd-receiving heirs their shares first
D) Divide the estate into shares based on the number of heirs

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, when a spouse and other fixed-share heirs are present, the spouse takes their fixed share from the smallest base, and the remainder is radded among the other heirs; the spouse never participates in radd.

Calculating Shares with Radd: One Category of Non-Radd Heirs
Explains the method for radd when one category of heirs does not receive radd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of an estate when one category of heirs (like a spouse) does not receive radd, using the Hanafi method of adjusting the base denominator.

Core Idea
When a spouse is present, the radd base is reduced to the spouse's share denominator.

In this lesson, we dive into a specific calculation method in the Hanafi school for faraid cases where radd applies but one group of heirs does not participate in the surplus. This is a common scenario, like when a husband or wife inherits alongside daughters. The method involves adjusting the base number to ensure integer shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the non-radd heir and their share denominator
Determine which heir does not receive radd (typically a spouse). Their prescribed share gives a denominator (makhraj), e.g., 1/4 gives 4.
Non-radd heirs are those excluded from receiving surplus, as per Hanafi rules.
2
Give the non-radd heir their share and examine the remainder
From the denominator, assign the non-radd heir their prescribed number of parts. The remainder is what will be distributed among the radd heirs.
Example: husband's share 1/4 from denominator 4, give him 1 part, remainder 3.
3
Check if the remainder divides evenly among the radd heirs' heads
Count the number of radd heirs (heads). See if the remainder is divisible by that number. If yes, the denominator stands; if not, proceed to the next step.
Divisibility means the remainder and heads share a common factor or are multiples.
4
Multiply heads by the denominator when there is disparity (mubayanah)
If the remainder and the number of heads are coprime (mubayanah), multiply the number of radd heirs by the non-radd denominator to obtain the new base.
Example: 3 remainder and 5 heads are coprime, so multiply 5 * 4 = 20.
5
Distribute using the new base
The non-radd heir receives their share from the new base (multiply original denominator portion by the multiplier, if any). The remainder goes to the radd heirs proportionally.
From base 20, husband gets 5 (1/4 of 20), daughters get 15 total, each 3.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Regarding the denominator of the one who does not receive radd, like a husband and six daughters. Otherwise, multiply all their heads by the denominator of the one who does receive radd. The prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd, like a husband and five daughters. Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on Faraid, specifically on the method of distributing shares when there are heirs who do not receive the radd (return of surplus) and those who do. The text is a commentary on a matn (likely from Kanz al-Daqa’iq). It begins by stating the rule: When there is one category of heirs who do not receive radd (such as a spouse) and one category who do (such as daughters), give the spouse their share, and if the remainder does not divide evenly among the radd recipients, multiply the number of their heads by the denominator of the spouse’s share to get the new base. Then it provides an example: a husband and five daughters. The husband’s share is one-fourth, denominator 4, leaving 3. This 3 does not divide among 5 daughters, so multiply 5 by 4 to get 20. The estate is divided from 20. The commentator notes that the original base was 12 (due to 1/4 and 2/3), but in radd, the base is reduced to the spouse’s denominator, here 4. This is a concise statement of the Hanafi method for radd with one category of non-radd heirs.

Key Terms
الردّ (ar-radd): Return of surplus to heirs who have prescribed shares (ashab al-furud) when there is no asabah.
مخرج (makhraj): The denominator of a prescribed share (fard), e.g., 4 for 1/4.
مباينة (mubayanah): Disparity between two numbers where neither divides the other, i.e., they are coprime.
رؤوس (ru'us): Heads; the number of individuals in a category of heirs.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, when a non-radd heir (like a spouse) is present with radd heirs, the final base denominator is obtained by multiplying the number of radd heirs by the denominator of the non-radd heir's share if the remainder does not divide evenly.

Radd with Two Categories of Heirs
Explains radd with two categories of heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the estate division when radd recipients belong to two or more categories, applying the Hanafi method of adjusting heads for each category.

Core Idea
When radd heirs are of two categories, ensure the remainder fits the total shares, then adjust each category's heads individually.

This passage extends the radd method to cases where the radd recipients consist of two distinct groups, such as grandmothers and maternal sisters. The example shows how to find a common base (makhraj) that accounts for both categories' head counts, even when the prescribed shares sum matches the remainder but individual portions do not divide evenly.

Guided Path
1
Separate non-radd heir
Identify any heir who does not receive radd (e.g., spouse). Determine their prescribed share and its denominator (makhraj). Subtract their portion from the estate; the remainder is for radd recipients.
In the example, wife gets 1/4, remainder = 3/4.
2
Check fit of remainder to radd groups' shares
Sum the prescribed shares of the radd groups (e.g., maternal sisters 1/3, grandmothers 1/6) and compare to the remainder. If they match (here both 3/12), the remainder fits.
Maternal sisters: 2 shares, grandmothers: 1 share, total 3 shares, matching remainder of 3 from wife's denominator 4.
3
Adjust each category's heads separately
For each radd group, compare the number of heads to the number of shares they receive. If they share a common divisor (muwafaqa), reduce the heads accordingly; if not (mubayana), keep heads intact. Here grandmothers: 1 share for 4 heads → disparity, keep 4; sisters: 2 shares for 6 heads → agreement by half, reduce to 3.
Seeking 'agreement' means the ratio of heads to shares can be simplified.
4
Find common multiplier between groups
If the reduced head counts of the groups are not directly adjustable, multiply the compatible number (wafq) of one group by the head count of the other to get a common multiple.
Here sisters' reduced heads = 3, grandmothers' heads = 4, no agreement → multiply 3 × 4 = 12.
5
Multiply by non-radd denominator
Multiply the result from step 4 by the denominator of the non-radd heir's share to get the final base of the estate. Then distribute accordingly.
12 × 4 = 48, so estate is divided into 48 parts.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مع الثاني من لا يردّ عليه، فاقسم ما بقي من مخرج فرض من لا يردّ عليه على مسألة من يردّ عليه كزوجة وأربع جدات وست أخوات الأم، فإن أقل مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه أربعة فإذا أعطيت الزوجة واحدا منها بقيت ثلاثة، وهي مستقيمة على مسألة من يرد عليه؛ لأنها أيضا ثلاثة؛ لأن حق الأخوات لأم الثلث، وحق الجدات السدس، فللأخوات سهمان وللجدات سهم واحد، ففي هذه الصورة استقام الباقي على مسألة من يرد عليه، لكن نصيب الجدات لا يستقيم على عدد رؤوسهن فإنه واحد بل بينهما مباينة، فحفظنا عدد رؤوسهن بأسرها. وكذا نصيب الأخوات الست لا يستقيم فإنه اثنان وبين عددي رؤوسهن وسهامهن موافقة بالنصف، فرددنا عدد رؤوس الأخوات إلى نصفها وهو ثلاثة، ثم طلبنا التوافق بين أعداد الرؤوس والرؤوس، فلم نجده، فضربنا وفق رؤوس الأخوات وهو الثلاثة في كل عدد رؤوس الجدات، وهو الأربعة، فحصل اثنا عشر، ثم ضربناها في الأربعة التي هو مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه فصار ثمانية وأربعين ومنها تصح المسألة، واعلم أن الاستقراء دل على أنه لا توجد مسألة ردية فيها أربع طوائف ولهذا اكتفينا باجتماع جنسين. (ملتقطا من شرح السراجية)
And if there is a second [category] of the one who does not receive radd, then divide what remains from the denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd by the problem of the one who receives radd, like a wife and four grandmothers and six maternal sisters. The smallest denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd is four. When you give the wife one, three remain. This three is commensurate with the problem of the one who receives radd because it is also three, since the right of the maternal sisters is one-third and the right of the grandmothers is one-sixth. For the sisters, two shares, and for the grandmothers, one share. In this scenario, the remainder fits the problem of the one who receives radd, but the portion of the grandmothers does not fit their number of heads because it is one; there is disparity between them. So we keep the number of their heads intact. Likewise, the portion of the six sisters does not fit; it is two, and between their number of heads and their shares is agreement by half. So we reduce the number of heads of the sisters to half, which is three. Then we seek agreement between the numbers of heads and heads, and find none. So we multiply the compatible number of the sisters, i.e., three, by the entire number of heads of the grandmothers, i.e., four, resulting in twelve. Then we multiply this by four, which is the denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd, making forty-eight, and from this the problem is valid. Know that induction shows that there is no radd problem with four groups, so we suffice with two groups. (Excerpt from Sharh al-Sirajiyyah)

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on radd, now addressing the case where the radd recipients are from two distinct categories (e.g., grandmothers and maternal sisters). The example given is a wife (non-radd), four grandmothers, and six maternal sisters. The wife’s share is 1/4, denominator 4, remainder 3. The combined shares of the radd groups also total 3 (sisters 2, grandmothers 1), so the remainder exactly equals the sum of their prescribed shares. However, individual portions do not divide evenly among the heads: grandmothers: 1 share for 4 heads (disparity); sisters: 2 shares for 6 heads (agreement by half). The commentator explains the process of finding a common basis: reduce the sisters’ heads to 3 (half), then multiply by grandmothers’ heads (4) to get 12, then multiply by the wife’s denominator (4) to get 48. This 48 becomes the base for the division. The passage notes that no radd case involves four groups, so the method covers up to three groups (here two categories of radd heirs). This is a practical demonstration of the Hanafi method for handling multiple radd categories.

Key Terms
الموافقة (al-muwafaqah): Agreement between two numbers, i.e., they share a common factor greater than 1.
الوفق (al-wafq): The compatible number (i.e., the quotient after dividing by the common divisor).
الجنسان (al-jinsan): Two categories or types of heirs.

Key Takeaway
When radd heirs span two categories, the final estate base is obtained by separately adjusting head counts for each category and then multiplying by the non-radd heir's denominator.

Radd with Non-Divisible Remainder: Cross-Multiplication Method
Explains radd when remainder does not match radd groups' shares.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a non-radd heir's remainder does not divide evenly among multiple radd groups, applying the Hanafi method of multiplying denominators.

Core Idea
When the remainder does not match the radd groups' shares, multiply non-radd denominator by radd mas'alah.

In some radd cases, after giving the non-radd heir their prescribed share, the remainder does not match the sum of the radd groups' prescribed shares. This lesson explains the Hanafi method to find a common base that works for both groups, using an example with wives, daughters, and grandmothers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the non-radd heir and reduce the base
Determine which heir(s) do not receive radd (e.g., spouse). Reduce the original estate denominator to the smallest denominator of their prescribed share.
In the example, wives have 1/8, so denominator 8.
2
Give the non-radd heir their share and find remainder
From the reduced base, give the non-radd heir their fraction. The remainder is what the radd groups will divide.
Wives get 1 part from 8, leaving 7 parts.
3
Determine the radd groups' mas'alah
Calculate the combined shares of the radd groups as a single fraction. Its denominator (the sum of their shares) is the mas'alah.
Daughters 4 parts, grandmothers 1 part = mas'alah 5.
4
Check divisibility of remainder on mas'alah
If the remainder does not divide evenly by the mas'alah, the shares cannot be distributed directly. Multiply the non-radd heir's denominator by the mas'alah to get a new common base.
7 does not divide 5, so multiply 8 × 5 = 40.
5
Distribute from the new base
The non-radd heir gets their fraction of the new base (1/8 of 40 = 5). The remainder (35) is divided among radd groups according to their mas'alah shares.
Daughters: 4/5 × 35 = 28; grandmothers: 1/5 × 35 = 7.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يستقم إلخ أي وإن لم يستقم ما بقي من مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه على مسألة من يرد عليه، فاضرب سهام من يرد عيه في مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه فحاصل هذا الضرب يكون مخرجا لفروض من يرد عليه ومن لا يرد عليه، كأربع زوجات وتسع بنات وست جدات، فإن أصل هذه المسألة . أربعة وعشرين لكنها ردية من فرددناها إلى أقل مخارج فرض من لا يرد عليه، وهو الثمانية، فإذا دفعنا ثمنها، وهو ثلاثة إلى الزوجات بقيت سبعة ولا تستقيم على الخمسة التي هي مساله من يرد عليه ههنا لأن الفرضين ثلثان وسدس بل بينهما مباينة في الثمانية يبلغ أربعين فهذا المبلغ مخرج فروض الفريقين. ثم اضرب إلخ أي ثم إذا أردت أن تعرف حصة كل فريق منهما من هذا المبلغ الذي هو مخرج فروضهما، فاضرب سهام من لا يرد عليه من أقل مخارج فرضه في مسألة من يرد عليه فيكون الحاصل نصيب من لا يرد عليه من المبلغ المذكور، فاضرب سهام كل فريق ممن يرد عليه من مسألتهم فيما بقي من مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه، فيكون الحاصل نصيب ذلك الفريق ممن يرد عليه، بيان الأول: أن المسألة المذكورة للزوجات المخرج واحد، فإذا ضربناه في الخمسة التي مسألة من يرد عليه كان الحاصل خمسة فهي حق الزوجات من الأربعين، وبيان الثاني: أن للبنات من مسألة من يرد عليه أربعة فإذا ضربناها فيما بقي من مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه وهو سبعة بلغ ثمانية وعشرين فهي لهن من الأربعين، وللجدات من . مسألة من يرد عليه واحد، فإذا ضربناه في السبعة كان سبعة فهي للجدات فقد استقام بهذا العمل فرض من لا يرد عليه، وفرض كل فريق ممن يرد عليه. (شرح السراجية بتصرف محشي)
And if it does not divide evenly etc., i.e., if what remains from the denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd does not divide evenly on the problem of the one who receives radd, then multiply the shares of the one who receives radd by the denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd. The result of this multiplication becomes the denominator for the prescribed shares of both groups. For example: four wives, nine daughters, and six grandmothers. The base of this problem is twenty-four, but it is a radd problem, so we reduce it to the smallest denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd, which is eight. When we give them one-eighth, i.e., three, to the wives, seven remain. This seven does not divide evenly on the five, which is the problem of the one who receives radd here, because the prescribed shares are two-thirds and one-sixth. Rather, there is disparity between them. Multiplying the eight gives forty; that amount is the denominator for the prescribed shares of the two groups. Then multiply etc.: i.e., when you want to know the share of each group from this amount, which is the denominator of their prescribed shares, multiply the shares of the one who does not receive radd from the smallest denominator of his prescribed share by the problem of the one who receives radd. The product will be the portion of the one who does not receive radd from the mentioned amount. Then multiply the shares of each group among the one who receives radd from their problem by what remains from the denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd; the product will be the portion of that group among the one who receives radd. Explanation of the first: the mentioned problem for the wives has one denominator; when we multiply it by five, which is the problem of the one who receives radd, the product is five, which is the right of the wives from the forty. Explanation of the second: for the daughters, from the problem of the one who receives radd, there are four shares; when we multiply them by what remains from the denominator of the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd, i.e., seven, it becomes twenty-eight, which is for them from the forty. For the grandmothers, from the problem of the one who receives radd, there is one share; when we multiply it by seven, it becomes seven, which is for the grandmothers. Thus, by this operation, the prescribed share of the one who does not receive radd and the prescribed share of each group among the one who receives radd are satisfied. (From Sharh al-Sirajiyyah with modifications by the commentator)

So the text might be mixing the original and reduced bases. The commentator later says the total makhraj for both groups is 40. Let's derive: For the four wives, they get 1/8 of the estate, which in terms of shares is 1 part from an 8-part estate? Actually the correct method: The non-radd heirs (wives) get their prescribed fraction of the total estate. Then the radd heirs divide the remainder according to their prescribed shares. If the remainder does not match the sum of their prescribed shares, we adjust by multiplying. Here, the wives' share denominator is 8, meaning the estate is divided into 8 parts. The wives get 1 part (1/8), leaving 7 parts. But the radd heirs' prescribed shares (daughters 2/3, grandmothers 1/6) when combined = 2/3 + 1/6 = 5/6 = 20/24, not 5/6 of 7 parts? To match, we need a common denominator. The text says the radd groups' total prescribed shares in terms of their problem (mas'alah) is 5 (daughters 4, grandmothers 1) from a common denominator? Actually the radd heirs' mas'alah (i.e., the sum of their fractions) is: daughters 2/3 = 8/12, grandmothers 1/6 = 2/12, total 10/12 = 5/6. Their mas'alah in terms of a common denominator would be 5 out of 6? But the text says 'الخمسة التي هي مساله من يرد عليه' – the five which is the problem of the one who receives radd. So they have a mas'alah of 5 (meaning their combined shares sum to 5 parts from a denominator of 6? Or from a denominator of 12? The commentary indicates: For the daughters, from the mas'alah of radd, they have 4 shares; for grandmothers, 1 share. So the radd groups' mas'alah is 5 (4+1). The wives' share is 1/8, which in the estate denominator of 8 is 1 part, leaving 7 parts. The radd groups' shares are 5 parts (but from a different denominator). So to distribute the 7 parts among the radd groups according to their ratio (4:1), we need to multiply the wives' denominator (8) by the radd groups' mas'alah (5) to get 40. This 40 becomes the common base. The wives get 1/8 of 40 = 5. The remainder is 35. The radd groups get: daughters 4/5 of 35 = 28; grandmothers 1/5 of 35 = 7. This matches the text. So the key lesson is: when the remainder does not align, multiply the non-radd heir's denominator by the radd groups' mas'alah (the number of shares they would have in their own distribution) to get a new base that accommodates both. The passage then explains how to find each group's share from this base.

Key Terms
مسألة من يرد عليه (mas'alatu man yuraddu 'alayhi): The problem or combined shares of the radd recipients, representing the sum of their prescribed fractions.
مخرج الفريقين (makhraj al-fariqayn): The common denominator for both the non-radd and radd groups, derived by multiplying the non-radd's denominator by the radd groups' mas'alah.
الردّ إلى أقل مخرج (ar-radd ila aqli makhraj): Reducing the base to the smallest denominator of the non-radd heir's prescribed share.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method for radd when the remainder does not divide evenly multiplies the non-radd heir's denominator by the radd groups' mas'alah to achieve a common base and proportional distribution.

Munasakhat: When Heirs Die Before Division
Definition and introduction of munasakhat in Hanafi faraid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define munasakhat and explain the transfer of a deceased heir's share to his own heirs before estate division.

Core Idea
An heir's share does not vanish at death — it is transferred to his own heirs.

Having completed the rules of radd (return of surplus), the author now turns to munasakhat — a distinct and practically important scenario in inheritance. When an heir dies before the estate is divided, his potential share does not lapse; instead, it passes to his own heirs. This lesson establishes the definition and core principle of this transfer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic root
Munasakhat is derived from naskh, meaning transfer or conversion. Here it refers to the transfer of an heir's share to his own heirs upon his death before division.
2
Understand the triggering scenario
The event is the death of a heir after the first death but before the estate of the first deceased is distributed. This creates a succession within the succession.
3
Distinguish from related concepts
Unlike radd (return of surplus to prescribed heirs) or tashih (correcting fractional shares), munasakhat deals with a new death that introduces a second layer of inheritance.
4
Recognize the practical effect
The deceased heir's share is not lost or redistributed to the original pool; it is inherited by his own heirs according to normal faraid rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات البعض قبل القسمة، أي بعض الورثة أي قبل قسمة التركة. لما فرغ من مسائل الرد شرع في مسائل المناسخة، وهي مفاعلة من النسخ بمعنى النقل والتحويل، والمراد بها هنا أن ينتقل نصيب بعض الورثة بموته قبل القسمة إلى من يرث منه. بعض الأنصباء ميراثا قبل القسمة، فإن كانت ورثة الميت الثاني هم ورثة الميت الأول، ولم يتغير طريق القسمة
And if some die before division, i.e., some of the heirs, before division of the estate. When he finished with the issues of radd, he began with the issues of munasakhat. It is a reciprocal form from al-naskh meaning transfer and conversion. What is meant here is that the share of some heirs by death before division is transferred to those who inherit from him. Some portions are inherited before division. If the heirs of the second deceased are the heirs of the first deceased and the method of division does not change.

Commentary
This short passage marks the transition from the topic of radd (return) to munasakhat (inheritance by successive deaths). The term munasakhat is derived from naskh meaning transfer; in this context, it refers to the situation where a heir dies before the estate is divided, and his share passes to his own heirs. The commentator notes that the discussion now covers how to handle such cases, especially when the heirs of the second deceased are the same as the first (e.g., a grandson dies before division, and the same set of heirs inherit from both). The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the general principle is clear: the division must account for the succession. This is a distinct subtopic in Hanafi faraid.

Key Terms
المناسخة (al-munasakhat): The transfer of a deceased heir's share to his own heirs before the original estate is divided.
النقل (an-naql): Transfer of the right of inheritance from the first deceased to the second deceased's heirs.

Munasakhat is the principle that a deceased heir's share is transferred to his own heirs, not redistributed among the original heirs.

Distributing Surplus (Radd) with Mixed Heir Groups
Explains the rule for combining radd and non-radd groups in faraid calculations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of an estate when both radd and non-radd heirs coexist, following the Hanafi method.

Core Idea
When radd and non-radd heirs coexist, find a common base, allocate non-radd shares, then distribute the remainder proportionally among radd heirs.

This passage from the commentary on al-Sirajiyya explains how to handle an estate where some heirs (like spouses) do not receive the surplus (radd) and others (like daughters and grandmothers) do. The Hanafi school provides a systematic procedure to ensure that each group receives its correct share. We will walk through that procedure with a detailed example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups
Separate heirs into two groups: those who do not receive radd (e.g., spouses) and those who do (e.g., children, parents, etc.). Only the latter participate in the radd distribution.
Spouses are permanently excluded from radd in the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the base (makhraj) for each group
For the non-radd group, take the denominator of their prescribed share (e.g., 1/4 gives base 4). For the radd group, combine their shares as if they were the only heirs and calculate the base for that combined fraction.
In the example, wives get 1/4; daughters and grandmothers together get the remainder after the wife, but for radd purposes their base is 5 (since after radd they share 4/5 and 1/5 respectively).
3
Find the common denominator
Multiply the bases of the two groups to get a common denominator. This is the starting total for the estate.
If the non-radd base is 4 and radd base is 5, the common denominator is 20. However, corrections may adjust this number.
4
Allocate the non-radd group's share
Calculate the non-radd group's share from the common denominator by multiplying their base (in reduced form) by the radd group's base. Then the remainder is for the radd group.
In the example, wives' share from 40 is 5 (since 1/4 of 40 = 10? Actually the text says 5, indicating a different adjustment).
5
Distribute the remainder among radd heirs proportionally
The radd group's share is the remainder after non-radd. Divide this remainder among the radd heirs according to their shares within the radd group (as if radd applied only to them).
In the example, daughters get 4/5 of the remainder and grandmothers 1/5, resulting in 28 and 7 out of 40 respectively.

The shares of the six grandmothers from it were seven, and between them also there is disparity, so we took all their heads. Commentary
This passage explains the method of distributing the estate when there are heirs who are not entitled to receive the surplus (radd), such as spouses, and heirs who are entitled to receive the surplus, such as daughters and grandmothers. The rule is: First, determine the base number for the shares of each group. For those who do not receive radd (e.g., wives), their base is the denominator of their share (e.g., 1/4 gives base 4). For those who receive radd (e.g., daughters and grandmothers), their base is the denominator of their combined shares after radd (here the base is 5 from 1/3 and 1/6). Then, multiply the base of the non-radd group by the base of the radd group to get a common denominator. Allocate the non-radd group's share from this common denominator, and then distribute the remainder to the radd heirs according to their proportions. If the resulting shares do not divide evenly among the heads of each group, apply the standard correction methods (the seven principles) to find a common multiple. The example given: Four wives (non-radd), nine daughters, and six grandmothers (both radd). The base for wives is 4, for radd group is 5, common denominator 20. But wait, the text says 40? Actually, the process: wives' base 1 (since 1/4 reduces to 1 in makhraj? Actually, the makhraj for wives is 4, but when combined, they use a different method. Follow the text: they take the smallest makhraj for wives (4) and multiply by radd group base (5) to get 20, but then they adjust? The text says the total becomes 40. This is a detailed example of the correction process. The teacher should walk through the steps: multiply, check compatibility, adjust, ultimately arriving at 1440 as the corrected base. The key takeaway is the systematic approach to handling multiple groups with different radd statuses.

Key Terms
رد (radd): The return of the surplus of the estate to the heirs in proportion to their shares after the prescribed shares are given, when there is no residuary heir.
مخارج الفروض (makharij al-furud): The denominators of the prescribed shares (e.g., 2, 3, 4, 6, 8, 12) used to calculate the base number of the estate.
فريق (fariq): A group of heirs with similar status regarding radd (either those to whom radd is returned or those to whom it is not returned).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When radd and non-radd heirs coexist, first find a common denominator, allocate non-radd shares, then distribute the remainder proportionally among radd heirs, correcting if shares do not divide evenly.

The Three States in Munasakhah: Identity, Compatibility, and Disparity
Explains the procedure and three states of munasakhah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three relationships between the share of a deceased heir and the base of their own estate, and apply the correct arithmetic procedure for each.

Core Idea
When an heir dies before division, combine their share with their own heirs' shares using identity, compatibility, or disparity.

Munasakhah arises when one or more heirs pass away before the estate is distributed. Instead of recalculating from scratch, the Hanafi method handles this by treating the deceased heir's share as a new estate for their own heirs. The key is the numerical relationship between that share and the base of the second estate. This lesson introduces the three relationships—identity, compatibility, and disparity—and the corresponding operations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic procedure of munasakhah
First correct the first estate (tas'hih) and assign shares. Then treat the deceased heir's share as a new estate and correct that for their heirs. Then compare the deceased heir's share (from first correction) with the base of the second correction.
The first correction's share becomes like the 'shares' and the second correction's base becomes like 'heads'.
2
Identify the three numerical relationships
Look at the ratio between the deceased heir's share (from first correction) and the base of the second correction. There are three possibilities: identity (mumathala) meaning exact division with no remainder; compatibility (muwafaqa) meaning they share a common factor; disparity (mubayana) meaning they are coprime.
Memorize the Arabic terms: مماثلة, موافقة, مباينة.
3
Apply the correct operation for identity
If the share aligns exactly with the second base (i.e., share equals base or is a multiple that gives the same result), no multiplication is needed. The final distribution is valid from the first correction's base.
Example: first estate base 6, sister's share 2; second estate base 2. Since 2 aligns with 2, no multiplication.
4
Apply the correct operation for compatibility
If share and base have a common factor, multiply the compatible part of the second base (base divided by common factor) by the entire first correction (the number of shares or the base). The result is the new combined base.
Example: wife, sister, five uncles. Sister's share 10, second base? The text gives partial example.
5
Apply the correct operation for disparity
If share and base have no common factor, multiply the entire second correction base by the first correction base (or by the share? The rule is multiply second base by first correction). The text's example is incomplete.
Standard Hanafi rule: if mubayanah, multiply the second base by the first correction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات البعض قبل القسمة، أي بعض الورثة أي قبل قسمة التركة = سبعة ولا تستقيم على الخمسة التي هي مساله من يرد عليه ههنا لأن الفرضين ثلثان وسدس بل بينهما مباينة في الثمانية يبلغ أربعين فهذا المبلغ مخرج فروض الفريقين. واعلم المسألة أنه ذا صار = فصحح مسألة الميت الأول واعط سهام كل وارث، ثم صحح مسألة الميت الثاني على ورثته فانظر بين ما في يده من التصحيح الأول وبين التصحيح الثاني ثلاثة أحوال فإن استقام ما في يده من التصحيح الأول على التصحيح الثاني، فلا ضرب، وصحتا من تصحيح الميت الأول، وإن لم يستقم، - فإنه يقسم المال حينئذ قسمة واحدة ولا حاجة إلى قسمة جديدة؛ إذ لا فائدة في تكرارها كما إذا ترك ابنين وبنات من امرأة واحدة ثم مات إحدى البنات ولا وارث لها سوى الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم، فإنه يقسم مجموع التركة بين الباقي للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين قسمة واحدة كما تقسم بين الجميع كذلك، فكأن الميت الثاني لم يكن أصلا في البين، وإن تغير طريق القسمة بين الباقين كما إذا ترك ابنا وثلاث بنات من امرأة أخرى ثم ماتت إحدى البنات قبل القسمة عن الأخ لأب والأختين لأبوين، فإن الثلثين لهما بالفرض، والباقي له بالتعصيب، أو كانت ورثة الميت الثاني غير ورثة الميت الأول فحكمه ما بينه بقوله: "فصحح مسألة الميت الأول إلخ"، هذا حاصل ما في "الفتح" و"شرح السراجية". فصحح إلخ: أي فصحح مسألة الأول بالقواعد السابقة على ورثته واعط سهام كل وارث من الصحيح، مسألة الميت الثاني على ورثته فانظر إلخ أي بعد تصحيح مسألة الميت الثاني انظر بين ما في يده من التصحيح الأول، وهو نصيب الميت الأول وبين التصحيح الثاني ثلاثة أحوال هي المماثلة، والموافقة، والمباينة والأصل أن التصحيح الأول هنا بمنزلة أصل المسألة، وما في يد الميت الثاني بمنزلة السهام والتصحيح الثاني بمنزلة الرؤوس. ملتقط من شرح السراجية وغيره) فإن استقام إلخ: أي فإن استقام بسبب المماثلة ما في يده من التصحيح الأول على التصحيح الثاني فلا حاجة إلى الضرب، وصحت الفريضتان من تصحيح الميت الأول؛ صورته رجل مات وترك بنتا، وأما وأختا لأب، ثم ماتت الأخت قبل القسمة وترك أما وزوجا، فمسألة الميت الأول من ستة للبنت النصف ثلاثة أسهم، وللأم السدس سهم، والباقي سهمان للأخت؛ لأن البنت عصبتها، ومسألة الميت الثاني من اثنين للزوج النصف سهم، والباقي وهو سهم للأم فرضا وردا، فاستقام ما في يد الأخت على مسألتها من غير ضرب وصحتا من ستة. (فتح، تكملة) وصحتا: أي الفريضتان فريضة الميت الأول وفريضة الميت الثاني. وإن لم يستقم إلخ: أي وإن لم يستقم ما في يده من التصحيح الأول على التصحيح الثاني فانظر إن كان بينهما موافقة فاضرب وفق التصحيح الثاني في جميع التصحيح الأول وصورته رجل مات وترك زوجة وأختا لأب وخمسة أعمام أصل المسألة. من أربعة للزوجة الربع وللأخت سهمان، وللأعمام الباقي، وهو سهم، وهو لا يستقيم عليهم، فاضرب رؤوسهم في أصل المسألة سهم، تبلغ عشرين للزوجة خمسة، وللأخت عشرة وللأعمام خمسة، ثم ماتت الأخت وتركت زوجا وأما وبنتا وعما، -
And if some die before the division, i.e., some of the heirs before the division of the estate = seven and does not align with the five which is the case of those to whom radd is returned here because the two shares are two-thirds and a sixth, but between them there is disparity in the eight which reaches forty, so this amount is the base of the shares of the two groups. And know that the case becomes: so correct the case of the first deceased and give the shares of each heir, then correct the case of the second deceased for his heirs, then look between what is in his hand from the first correction and the second correction: three states. If what is in his hand from the first correction aligns with the second correction, then no multiplication, and both are correct from the correction of the first deceased. And if it does not align, then the property is divided in one division and there is no need for a new division, as when someone leaves two sons and daughters from one wife, then one of the daughters dies and she has no heir except the brothers and sisters from the father and mother. Then the total estate is divided among the remaining, with the male having the share of two females, one division, as it would be divided among all, as if the second deceased was not in the picture. And if the method of division changes among the remaining, as when someone leaves a son and three daughters from another wife, then one of the daughters dies before division, leaving a brother from the father and two sisters from both parents. Then two-thirds are for them by prescribed share, and the remainder is for him by residuary. Or if the heirs of the second deceased are different from the heirs of the first deceased, then its ruling is what he stated: 'Correct the case of the first deceased etc.' This is the gist of what is in al-Fath and Sharh al-Sirajiyya. 'Correct etc.' means correct the case of the first with the previous rules for his heirs and give each heir his shares from the correction. Then correct the case of the second deceased for his heirs, and look etc. After correcting the case of the second deceased, look between what is in his hand from the first correction, which is the share of the first deceased, and the second correction: three states: identical, compatible, and disparate. The principle is that the first correction here is like the base of the case, what is in the hand of the second deceased is like the shares, and the second correction is like the heads. (Taken from Sharh al-Sirajiyya and others) 'If it aligns etc.' means if due to identity what is in his hand from the first correction aligns with the second correction, then no need for multiplication, and both shares are correct from the correction of the first deceased. Its example: a man died leaving a daughter, a mother, and a sister from the father. Then the sister died before division, leaving a mother and a husband. The case of the first deceased is from six: for the daughter half, three shares; for the mother one-sixth, one share; the remainder two shares for the sister because the daughter is her residuary. The case of the second deceased is from two: for the husband half, one share; the remainder which is one share for the mother by prescribed share and radd. So what was in the hand of the sister aligned with her case without multiplication, and both are correct from six. (Fath, Completion) 'And both are correct' means the two shares: the share of the first deceased and the share of the second deceased. 'And if it does not align etc.' means if what is in his hand from the first correction does not align with the second correction, then look: if between them there is compatibility, multiply the compatible part of the second correction by all of the first correction. Its example: a man died leaving a wife, a sister from the father, and five uncles. The base of the case is from four: for the wife one-fourth, one share; for the sister two shares; for the uncles the remainder which is one share, but it does not align upon them. So multiply their heads by the base of the case, one share, becoming twenty: for the wife five, for the sister ten, for the uncles five. Then the sister died leaving a husband, a mother, a daughter, and an uncle -
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage introduces the rules of munasakhah (subsequent deaths before division of the estate). When one or more heirs die before the estate is divided, their shares must be redistributed to their own heirs. The ruling depends on the relationship between the original heirs and the new heirs. There are three cases: (1) Identity (mumathala): when the share of the deceased heir aligns exactly with his new heirs' shares without adjustment. Example: first estate had daughter, mother, sister; sister died leaving mother and husband; sister's share (2) equals what her heirs get from her estate (2 from base 6), so no adjustment. (2) Compatibility (muwafaqa): when there is a common factor between the share and the new base, requiring multiplication by the agreed part. Example: first estate with wife, sister, five uncles; sister's share (10) and her estate's base (?) need adjustment. The text gives an example but cuts off. (3) Disparity (mubayana): when there is no common factor, requiring multiplication of the entire second base by the first correction. The passage also notes a special case where if the second deceased's heirs are the same as the first's, and the method of division does not change, the entire estate is divided in one go without separate calculation. The key procedure: correct the first estate, give each heir their shares; then treat the deceased heir's share as a new estate, correct it for his heirs, and then combine the two corrections by looking at the three relationships. The teacher should emphasize that this ensures accurate distribution without double counting.

Key Terms
منا سخة (munasakhah): The legal situation where one or more heirs die before the estate is divided, requiring the redistribution of their shares to their own heirs.
تصحيح (tas'hih): The process of finding a common base number so that all shares can be expressed as whole numbers without fractions.
مماثلة (mumathalah): Literal 'identity': when the share of the first deceased heir exactly matches the base of the second deceased's case, requiring no further multiplication.
موافقة (muwafaqah): Literal 'compatibility': when the share of the first deceased heir and the base of the second deceased's case share a common factor, allowing partial multiplication.
مباينة (mubayanah): Literal 'disparity': when the share of the first deceased heir and the base of the second deceased's case have no common factor, requiring full multiplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the identity example from the text, what is the final combined base number for both estates?
A) 6
B) 12
C) 2
D) 24

Key Takeaway
In munasakhah, the relationship between the deceased heir's share and the base of their own estate determines whether you multiply and by how much.

The Three Cases in Munasakhat (Progressive Inheritance)
Explains the three numerical relationships and multiplication rules for munasakhat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three relationships (istiqamah, muwafaqah, mubayanah) in munasakhat and apply the correct multiplication method to incorporate the second inheritance.

Core Idea
When an heir dies before distribution, check correspondence, congruence, or disparity to determine the multiplier.

Munasakhat occurs when an heir dies before the estate is fully distributed. The Hanafi school provides a systematic method to incorporate the second inheritance into the first. This lesson explains the three mathematical relationships and the corresponding operations to find the final shares of all heirs.

Guided Path
1
Correct the first case
Perform the initial tashih (correction) of the first deceased's estate, identifying the base number and each heir's share.
The share of the second deceased from this correction is the starting point.
2
Set up the second correction
Correct the case of the second deceased (who died before distribution) as if his inheritance were a new estate. Determine his heirs and their fractional shares, then find the base number for this second correction.
3
Compare the share to the new base
Take the share of the second deceased from the first correction and compare it to the base number of the second correction. Determine if there is istiqamah (exact correspondence), muwafaqah (common factor >1), or mubayanah (no common factor other than 1).
This step determines the operation needed.
4
Apply the multiplication rule
If istiqamah: no multiplication, the first correction stands. If muwafaqah: multiply the wafq (base of second correction divided by common factor) by the first correction. If mubayanah: multiply the entire base of the second correction by the first correction.
The result is the common denominator for both cases.
5
Adjust individual shares
Multiply the shares of the heirs of the first deceased (from the first correction) by the multiplier (second correction base or its wafq, depending on relationship), and similarly multiply the shares of the second deceased's heirs by the share of the second deceased from the first correction (or its wafq). The resulting products are their final shares in the common base.
Ensure each heir gets the correct portion of the total.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصحح مسألة الميت الأول واعط سهام كل وارث، ثم صحح على ورثته من الصحيح مسألة الميت الثاني، على ورثته فانظر بين ما في يده من التصحيح الأول وبين التصحيح الثاني ثلاثة أحوال فإن استقام ما في يده من التصحيح الأول على التصحيح الثاني، فلا ضرب، وصحتا من تصحيح الميت الأول، وإن لم يستقم، فإن كان بينهما موافقة فاضرب وفق التصحيح الثاني في كل التصحيح الأول، وإن كان بينهما مباينة، فاضرب كل التصحيح الثاني في التصحيح الأول، فالمبلغ مخرج المسألتين واضرب سهام ورثة الميت الأول من تصحيح في التصحيح الثاني إذا كان بين ما في يد الميت الثاني، وبين التصحيح الثاني مباينة أو في وفقه إن كان بينهما موافقة فيكون الحاصل من ضرب سهام كل وارث منهم في هذا المضروب نصيبه من المبلغ المذكور، وأيضا اضرب سهام ورثة الميت الثاني من تصحيح مسألته فيما في يد الميت الثاني من التصحيح الأول إن كان بينهما مباينة أو في وفقه إن كان بينهما موافقة فيكون الحاصل نصيبهم من المبلغ.
So correct the case of the first deceased and give the shares of each heir, then correct the case of the second deceased upon its heirs. Then look between what is in his hand from the first correction and the second correction: three states. If what is in his hand from the first correction is consistent with the second correction, then no multiplication, and both are correct from the correction of the first deceased. If not consistent, then if there is congruence between them, multiply the factor of the second correction by the entire first correction. If there is disparity, multiply the entire second correction by the entire first correction. The result is the common denominator of the two cases. And multiply the shares of the heirs of the first deceased from his correction by the second correction if there is disparity between what is in the hand of the second deceased and the second correction, or by its factor if there is congruence; thus the result of multiplying the shares of each heir by this multiplier is his share from the mentioned total. Also multiply the shares of the heirs of the second deceased from the correction of his case by what is in the hand of the second deceased from the first correction if there is disparity, or by its factor if there is congruence; thus the result is their shares from the total.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage explains the method of resolving inheritance when one or more heirs die before the distribution (munasakhat). The author, commenting on the matn, describes three possible relationships between the shares of the deceased second heir (from the first correction) and the denominators of the second correction: correspondence (istiqamah), congruence (tawafuq), and disparity (tabayun). If the shares fit exactly into the new denominators, no multiplication is needed. If they are congruent (share a common factor), multiply the reduced denominator of the second correction by the entire first correction. If they are disparate (no common factor), multiply the entire second correction by the entire first correction. The resulting product becomes the common base for both cases. Then, to find each heir's final share, multiply their shares from the first or second correction accordingly. The examples in the text illustrate these steps numerically.

Key Terms
مناسخة (munāsakhah): The situation where an heir dies before the distribution of the original estate, requiring a new calculation.
تصحيح (taṣḥīḥ): The process of correcting the fractions so that each heir's share is expressed in whole numbers without fractions.
موافقة (muwāfaqah): Congruence: when two numbers share a common factor greater than 1.
مباينة (mubāyanah): Disparity: when two numbers have no common factor other than 1.
استقامة (istiqāmah): Correspondence: when the shares from the first correction exactly match the denominators of the second correction without any remainder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the share of the second deceased from the first correction and the base of the second correction have no common factor other than 1, what operation should be performed?
A) Multiply the wafq of the second correction by the first correction.
B) Multiply the entire second correction by the entire first correction.
C) No multiplication is needed.
D) Multiply the shares by the square of the factor.

Key Takeaway
The relationship between the deceased heir's share and the second correction's base determines the multiplier: correspondence (none), congruence (factor), disparity (full).

Munasakhat: Combining Two Inheritance Cases
Rule for merging two inheritance cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method for combining two inheritance cases (munasakhat) by distinguishing between muwafaqa and mubayana and calculating the combined base and individual shares.

Core Idea
When merging inheritance cases, the multiplier depends on whether the numbers are coprime or share a common divisor.

In inheritance, when an heir dies before distribution, we must merge two cases. The Hanafi school has a precise computational method based on the numerical relationship between the shares. This lesson will guide you through the rule and its application, using a classic example from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases and their corrected bases
Determine the corrected base (tashih) for each case. For the first deceased, after adjusting for divisibility among heirs, you get a corrected base. For the second deceased, his own estate has a base number (often after tashih if needed).
In the example, first tashih = 12, second case base = 5.
2
Find the relationship between the second deceased's shares from case 1 and his own case base
Take the share that the second deceased received from the first inheritance (what is 'in his hand') and compare it with the base of his own case. Determine if they are coprime (mubayana, gcd=1) or share a common divisor (muwafaqa).
In the example, the wife held 3, and her case base is 5; gcd=1 → mubayana.
3
Apply the multiplication rule to get the combined base
If mubayana, multiply the full second base by the full first base. If muwafaqa, multiply the wafq (second base divided by gcd) by the full first base. The product is the common denominator for the merged case.
Here: 5 × 12 = 60.
4
Calculate shares of heirs who did not die
For heirs of the first deceased who survive, multiply their shares from the first tashih by the appropriate multiplier: the full second base (if mubayana) or its wafq (if muwafaqa). This gives their share in the combined base.
Sister's 6 × 5 = 30; uncles' 3 × 5 = 15.
5
Calculate shares of the second deceased's heirs
For heirs of the second deceased, take their shares from the second case's corrected base and multiply by what the second deceased held from the first case (if mubayana) or its wafq (if muwafaqa).
Brothers' 5 × 3 = 15 total, each of 5 gets 3.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان بينهما موافقة فاضرب وفق التصحيح الثاني في كل التصحيح الأول، وإن كان بينهما مباينة، فاضرب كل التصحيح الثاني في التصحيح الأول، فالمبلغ مخرج المسألتين واضرب سهام ورثة الميت الأول من تصحيحه في التصحيح الثاني إذا كان بين ما في يد الميت الثاني، وبين التصحيح الثاني مباينة أو في وفقه إن كان بينهما موافقة فيكون الحاصل من ضرب سهام كل وارث منهم في هذا المضروب نصيبه من المبلغ المذكور، وأيضا اضرب سهام ورثة الميت الثاني من تصحيح مسألته في كل ما في يد الميت الثاني على تقدير المباينة أو في وفقه على تقدير الموافقة. وصورته: رجل مات وترك زوجة، وأختا لأب، وثلاثة أعمام، فأصل المسألة أربعة للزوجة وللأخت لأب النصف سهمان، والباقي – وهو سهم – للأعمام وهو لا يستقيم عليهم، فاضرب كل رؤوسهم في أصل المسألة تبلغ اثني عشر : للزوجة ثلاثة وللأخت ستة وللأعمام ثلاثة، ثم ماتت الزوجة وتركت خمسة إخوة، ومسألتها من خمسة وما في يدها من التصحيح الأول - وهو ثلاثة - لا يستقيم على مسألتها ويباين، فيضرب كل التصحيح الثاني في التصحيح الأول يبلغ ستين، وهي مخرج المسألتين، كان للأخت لأب من الميت الأول ستة تضرب في التصحيح الثاني، وذلك خمسة تبلغ ثلاثين وكان للأعمام من الميت الأول ثلاثة تضرب في التصحيح الثاني، وذلك خمسة تبلغ خمسة عشر وكان للإخوة من الميت الثاني خمسة تضرب فيما في يده، وذلك ثلاثة تبلغ خمسة عشر، لكل ثلاثة.
If there is a common divisor between them, then multiply the half of the second correction (tashih) by the entire first correction. And if there is a coprime relationship between them, then multiply the entire second correction by the entire first correction. The resulting sum is the common denominator of the two cases. And multiply the shares of the heirs of the first deceased from his correction by the second correction if there is a coprime relationship between what is in the hand of the second deceased and the second correction, or by its equivalent (half) if there is a common divisor. Then the product of multiplying each heir's share in this multiplier is his portion from the said sum. Also multiply the shares of the heirs of the second deceased from the correction of his case by all that is in the hand of the second deceased in the case of coprime relationship, or by its half in the case of common divisor. And its example: A man died leaving a wife, a paternal sister, and three paternal uncles. The base of the case is four: the wife gets one, the paternal sister gets half (two shares), and the remainder (one share) goes to the uncles, but it is not divisible among them. So multiply the number of their heads by the base of the case, resulting in twelve: the wife gets three, the sister gets six, and the uncles get three. Then the wife died leaving five brothers. Her case base is five, and what is in her hand from the first correction (i.e., three) does not distribute evenly in her case and is coprime. So multiply all of the second correction by the first correction, resulting in sixty, which is the common denominator of the two cases. The paternal sister from the first deceased had six shares, multiplied by the second correction (five) gives thirty. The paternal uncles from the first deceased had three shares, multiplied by the second correction (five) gives fifteen. The brothers from the second deceased had five shares, multiplied by what was in his hand (three) gives fifteen, each gets three.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the method of combining two inheritance cases when a second heir dies before distribution (munasakhat). The author gives the rule: compare what the second deceased holds from the first case (his shares from the first deceased) with the total base number of his own case. If there is a common factor (muwafaqa), multiply the reduced second base (after dividing by the common factor) by the full first base. If they are coprime (mubayana), multiply the full second base by the full first base. The product is the combined base. Then to find each heir's share, multiply their shares from their corrected case by the appropriate multiplier (the second base or its half, and for heirs of the second deceased, multiply by what the second deceased held from the first case). Two examples illustrate both scenarios: in the first example (muwafaqa) the shares of the wife (3) and the second deceased's base (5) are not mentioned? Actually the first example given in the text is of muwafaqa earlier, and then the second example of mubayana is fully worked out. The teacher should note that this is a standard Hanafi method for multiple deaths, ensuring just distribution among all heirs of both cases. The passage is technical, typical of faraid manuals.

Key Terms
المناسخات (al-munasakhat): The situation where one or more heirs die before the estate of the original deceased is distributed, requiring multiple inheritance calculations to be combined.
وفق (wafq): The reduced number after dividing two numbers by their greatest common divisor (the half or matching part).
مباينة (mubāyana): The relationship between two numbers that have no common divisor other than 1 (coprime).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 60
C) 15
D) 5

Key Takeaway
Munasakhat requires comparing the second deceased's holdings with his own case base to choose the correct multiplier.

Computing Group and Individual Shares from the Corrected Base
Method to compute group and individual shares after tashih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compute the share of each group and each individual heir from the final corrected base using the multiplier method.

Core Idea
The group's share is its original share times the multiplier; each individual's share is the ratio of group shares to heads times the same multiplier.

In faraid, after correcting the base (tashih), you need to distribute the total estate among groups and then individuals. This lesson explains the two-step method: first find the total for each group, then find each person's share within that group, using the multiplier that links the original base to the corrected base.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original shares and the multiplier
From the corrected base, determine the multiplier 'm' that was used to expand the original base. Also note each group's original share (from the base before correction).
The multiplier is the same for all groups.
2
Compute group share
Multiply each group's original share by the multiplier 'm' to get the group's total share from the corrected base.
3
Compute the ratio of original shares to heads
For each group, divide the original shares of that group (from the original base) by the number of individuals in that group. This ratio represents the proportion per person.
This ratio is often left as a fraction.
4
Compute individual share
Multiply the ratio obtained in step 3 by the same multiplier 'm' to get the share of each individual in that group.
This is equivalent to dividing the group's total share by the number of individuals.

ويعرف حظ كل فريق من التصحيح بضرب ما لكل من أصل المسألة فيما ضربته في أصل المسألة. بيانه في المثال الذي ذكرناه في التصحيح عند قول المصنف وإلا فالعدد في العدد إلخ من اجتماع امرأتين وست جدات وعشر بنات وسبعة أعمام أنه إذا أردت أن تعرف نصيب كل فريق من مجموع ما حصل من الضرب وهو خمسة آلاف وأربعون فطريقه أن تأخذ نصيب المرأتين مثلا وهو أربعة وعشرون، ثم تضربها في مبلغ الضرب الذي ضربته في أصل المسألة الذي هو من أصل المسألة وهو مائتان وعشرة فما حصل من الضرب، وهو ستمائة وثلاثون نصيبهما، وكذا تأخذ نصيب البنات، وهو ستة عشر، ثم تضربها في المبلغ المذكور تحصل ثلاثة آلاف وثلاث مائة وستون، فهي نصيبهن، وكذا تضرب نصيب الجدات وهو أربعة في المبلغ تحصل ثمان مائة وأربعون فهي نصيبهن، وكذا تضرب نصيب الأعمام، وهو سهم في المبلغ تحصل مائتان وعشرة فهي نصيبهم فافهم واحفظ. وحظ كل فرد إلخ: يعني بعد معرفة حظ كل فريق من الورثة إذا أردت أن تعرف نصيب كل واحد من ذلك الفريق من التصحيح فيعرف ذلك بأن تنسب سهام كل فريق من أصل المسألة من عدد رؤوسهم منفردا عن أعداد رؤوسهم ثم تعطي لكل واحد من آحاد ذلك الفريق بمثل تلك النسبة من المضروب الذي ضربته في أصل وهو مائتان وعشرة في المثال المذكور، ففي المثال المذكور إذا نسبت سهام المرأتين وهي ثلاثة إليهما كانت النسبة مثلا ونصفا وإذا أعطيت كل واحدة منهما من المضروب المذكور بمثل تلك النسبة – أعني مثله ونصفه – كانت ثلاث مائة وخمسة عشر وإذا نسبت سهام البنات وهي ستة عشر إلى عدد رؤوسهن، وهو عشرة كانت النسبة مثلا وثلاثة أخماس مثل، فإذا أعطيت كل بنت مثل المضروب، ومثل ثلاثة أحماسه كانت لها ثلاث مائة وثلاثون، وإذا نسبت سهام الجدات وهي أربعة إلى عدد رؤوسهن، وهو ستة كانت النسبة ثلثي واحد، –
And the share of each group from the correction is known by multiplying what each had from the original base by what you multiplied in the original base. Its explanation is in the example we mentioned in the correction at the author's saying 'otherwise the number in the number etc.' concerning the gathering of two wives, six grandmothers, ten daughters, and seven uncles: if you want to know the share of each group from the total product of multiplication, which is five thousand and forty, then the method is to take the share of the two wives, for example, which is twenty-four, then multiply it by the amount of the multiplier that you multiplied in the original base, which is from the original base, i.e., two hundred and ten; what results from the multiplication, i.e., six hundred and thirty, is their share. Likewise, take the share of the daughters, which is sixteen, then multiply it by the said amount, yielding three thousand three hundred and sixty; that is their share. Likewise, multiply the share of the grandmothers, which is four, by the amount, yielding eight hundred and forty; that is their share. Likewise, multiply the share of the uncles, which is one share, by the amount, yielding two hundred and ten; that is their share. So understand and memorize. And the share of each individual etc.: meaning after knowing the share of each group of heirs, if you want to know the share of each one of that group from the correction, then that is known by relating the shares of each group from the original base to the number of their heads, separate from the numbers of their heads, then give each individual of that group a portion of the multiplier that you multiplied in the original, which is two hundred and ten in the mentioned example, in proportion to that ratio. So in the mentioned example, if you relate the shares of the two wives, which are three, to them, the ratio is one and a half; if you give each of them from the said multiplier according to that ratio – I mean one and a half times – it becomes three hundred and fifteen. And if you relate the shares of the daughters, which are sixteen, to the number of their heads, which is ten, the ratio is one and three-fifths; if you give each daughter the multiplier and three-fifths of it, then she has three hundred and thirty. And if you relate the shares of the grandmothers, which are four, to the number of their heads, which is six, the ratio is two-thirds; –

Commentary
This passage explains two procedures after the final corrected base (tashih) is found. First, to find the total share of a group (e.g., all wives together), multiply the group's original share from the base (before correction) by the multiplier that was used to expand the entire original base. In the example, the original base was unknown, but after correction the final base is 5040. The original shares: wives 24, daughters 16, grandmothers 4, uncles 1. The multiplier used to get from the original base to the final base is 210 (since 24*210=5040? Actually the final base is 5040, so the multiplier is 210). So each group's share is their original share times 210. Second, to find each individual's share within a group, find the ratio of the total shares of that group to the number of individuals in that group from the original assignment (before correction), then multiply that ratio by the same multiplier (210). For example, the two wives had 3 shares originally (out of an original base of 24? Wait, the text says original shares for wives are 3 from the original base? There's inconsistency: earlier the original shares for wives were 24, but here the ratio for individuals uses 3 shares for the two wives. Actually the example is from a different part of the text (the author's example with 'otherwise the number in the number'). The teacher should clarify: the original base before correction had specific shares per group; after correction, the base is multiplied. The method described here is standard: for each group, total share = original group share × multiplier; for each individual, share = (original shares of that group / number of individuals) × multiplier. The ratios given (one and a half, one and three-fifths, two thirds) come from dividing the original group shares by the number of heads. This is typical Hanafi faraid technique.

Key Terms
حظ الفريق (hazz al-farīq): The total share of a group of heirs (e.g., all wives, all daughters) from the corrected base after tashih.
نسبة (nisba): The ratio of the original shares of a group to the number of individuals in that group, used to compute individual shares.

Key Takeaway
Computing individual shares requires first finding the group's total share via the multiplier, then dividing proportionally using the ratio of original shares to heads.

Faraid — Inheritance

12 min
Calculating Group and Individual Shares from the Corrected Number
Explains how to find shares of groups and individuals after tashih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the total share of each group of heirs from the corrected number and determine the share of each individual within the group using the Hanafi proportional method.

Core Idea
Multiply each group's original share by the correction multiplier to get their total; then distribute proportionally among individuals.

After finding the corrected base number through tashih, you need to determine how much each group of heirs receives and then how much each individual in that group gets. This lesson walks through the Hanafi method described in the text: taking the group's share from the original problem, multiplying it by the correction multiplier, and then for individuals, comparing the group's share to the number of heads to find the proportion. The example with two wives, six grandmothers, ten daughters, and seven uncles illustrates the process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups and their original shares
From your asl al-mas'alah, list each group of heirs (e.g., wives, grandmothers, daughters, uncles) and note their combined share from that original problem. In the example, wives have 3 shares, grandmothers 4, daughters 16, uncles 1 (total 24).
2
Determine the correction multiplier
This is the number you multiplied the original problem by to get the corrected base (tashih). In the example, the multiplier is 210.
3
Calculate each group's total from the correction
Multiply each group's original share by the correction multiplier. For the wives: 3 × 210 = 630; for grandmothers: 4 × 210 = 840; for daughters: 16 × 210 = 3,360; for uncles: 1 × 210 = 210. These are the group's total shares from the corrected number.
4
Find each individual's share within a group using the ratio method
For each group, compare the group's original share to the number of individuals (ru'us). For wives: 3 shares for 2 wives → ratio 1.5 (3/2). Then give each wife that ratio times the correction multiplier: 1.5 × 210 = 315. Similarly, grandmothers: 4 shares for 6 → ratio 2/3 (0.666...), each gram: (2/3)×210 = 140. Daughters: 16 shares for 10 → ratio 1.6, each daughter: 1.6×210 = 336. Uncles: 1 share for 7 → ratio 1/7 ≈0.142857, each uncle: (1/7)×210 = 30.
Alternatively, you can divide the group's total from step 3 by the number of individuals: 630/2=315, etc.
5
Verify with alternative methods
The text mentions two other methods: (1) divide the group's original share by heads, then multiply by the multiplier; (2) divide the multiplier by the number of groups (not recommended). The ratio method is the clearest.

في التصحيح الثاني أو في وفقه وسهام ورثة الميت الثاني في نصيب الميت الثاني أو إن كان بينهما موافقة اضرب في وفقه، ويعرف حظ كل فريق من التصحيح بضرب ما لكل من أصل المسألة فيما عند الموافقة ضربته في أصل المسألة، وحظ كل فرد .يعرف حظ أي من أفراد الفريق ما كان أي لكل فريق سهام ورثة الميت الثاني من تصحيح مسألة في كل ما في يد الميت الثاني على تقدير المباينة أو في وفقه على تقدير الموافقة، فيكون الحاصل من ضرب سهام كل واحد منهم فيما ذكر نصيبه، وقد ذكرنا ذلك مفصلا عند كل من مثالي الموافقة والمباينة، فلا حاجة إلى الإعادة. التصحيح الثاني: إن كان بين ما في يد الميت الثاني وتصحيحه مباينة. (طائي) الميت الثاني: إن كان بين ما في يد الميت الثاني وتصحيحه مباينة. ويعرف إلخ: لما فرغ عن بيان صور التصحيح فيما قبل أراد أن يبين كيف يعرف نصيب كل فريق من الورثة من التصحيح الذي استقام على الكل فقال : " ويعرف إلخ"، وهذا لا تعلق له بمسالة المناسخة بل هو متعلق بمسألة التصحيح، ولذا قال في "التكملة": وهذه المسألة موضعها باب التصحيح.

بنسبة سهام كل فريق من أصل المسألة إلى عدد رؤوسهم مفرداي، ثم تعطى بمثل رؤوس ذلك الفريق حال كونه مفردا تلك النسبة من المضروب لكل فرد وإن أردت قسمة التركة بين الورثة أو الغرماء، فاضرب سهام = عدد رؤوسهم من أفراد الفريق من التركة. وإذا أعطيت كل واحدة منهن ثلثي المضروب كانت لها مائة وأربعون وإذا نسبت سهم الأعمام، وهو واحد إلى كانت النسبة سبع واحد، وإذا أعطيت كل واحد منهم سبع المضروب حصل له ثلاثون. بنسبة سهام كل فريق إلخ : هذا أوضح طرق معرفة حظ كل فرد لعدم الحاجة فيه إلى القسمة والضرب، وهناك وجهان آخران أحدهما أن يقسم ما كان لكل فريق من أصل المسألة على عدد رؤوسهم ثم يضرب الخارج من هذه القسمة في المضروب الذي ضربته في أصل المسألة لأجل التصحيح، فالحاصل من ضرب الخارج في المضروب نصيب كل واحد من آحاد ذلك الفريق، والثاني: أن تقسم المضروب أي العدد الذي ضربته في أصل المسألة للتصحيح على أي فريق شئت من فرق الورثة، ثم اضرب الخارج من هذه القسمة في نصيب الفريق الذي قسمت عليهم المضروب، فالحاصل من هذه الضرب نصيب كل واحد من آحاد ذلك الفريق. (فتح الله المعين) ثم تعطي كل واحد من آحاد الفريق وإن أردت قسمة التركة إلخ لما فرغ من تصحيح المسائل، وتعيين النصيب منه لكل فريق، ولكل واحد من الفريق شرع في بيان قسمة التركات بين الورثة والغرماء، وتعيين الأنصباء . (شرح السراجية بين الورثة أو الغرماء إلخ : أي إذا أردت قسمة التركة بين الورثة أو أردت قسمة التركة بين الغرماء وليس المراد أن تقسم التركة بين الورثة والغرماء بحسب الجمع كما يوهمه ما وقع في بعض النسخ: "والغرماء" بالواو مكان "أو الغرماء" لتقدم الغرماء على قسمة المواريث فلا يمكن الجمع بينهما. فاضرب سهام إلخ : هذا إذا كان بين التركة والتصحيح مباينة، مثلا إذا خلفت زوجا وأما وأختين لأب وأم كانت المسألة من ستة، وتعول إلى ثمانية، فللزوج منها ثلاثة وللأم واحد، ولكل واحدة من الأختين سهمان، فإن فرضنا أن جميع التركة خمسة وعشرون دينارا كانت بينهما وبين التصحيح الذي هو ثمانية مباينة، فإذا أردت أن تعرف نصيب كل وارث من هذه التركة فاضرب نصيب الزوج من التصحيح، وهو ثلاثة في كل التركة تحصل خمسة وسبعون ثم اقسم هذا المبلغ على التصحيح - أعني ثمانية – تخرج تسعة دنانير، وثلاثة أثمان دينار، فهذا نصيب الزوج من تلك التركة وكذلك اضرب نصيب الأم وهو الواحد في كل التركة تحصل خمسة وعشرون، ثم اقسم على الثمانية خرجت ثلاثة دنانير وثمن ،دينار، فهي نصيب الأم من التركة، وكذا اضرب نصيب كل أخت من التصحيح، وهو اثنان في كل التركة يحصل خمسون، فإذا قسمت هذا الحاصل على الثمانية خرجت ستة دنانير وربع دينار، فهي نصيب كل أخت من التركة، وإن كان بين التصحيح والتركة موافقة، فاضرب سهام كل وارث من التصحيح في وفق التركة ثم اقسم المبلغ الحاصل من الضرب على وفق التصحيح، فالخارج نصيب الوارث، وتفصيله في شرح السراجية.
